Order of Priority for Leading Funeral Prayer and the Wali's Right to Repeat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on janazah leadership order and i'adah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority for leading janazah and determine when the wali may repeat the prayer.

Core Idea
The wali has a right, but the sultan takes precedence; after the wali leads, no repetition is allowed.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer and whether the prayer can be repeated. The order of priority involves the sultan, local rulers, and the wali, with a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the majority. Understanding this order prevents confusion at funerals and resolves conflicts between family and authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Leading the funeral prayer (imamat al-janazah). Determine the overall hukm: it is fard kifayah, but the passage focuses on entitlement (haqq) rather than obligation.
The ruling on leading is not fard 'ayn; entitlement does not affect the obligation of the community.
2
List the order of priority
From the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad, extract the sequence: sultan → city ruler → judge → appointed governor → local imam → wali. Note that the wali is last in this order.
This order is preferred by most mashayikh and is the mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the wali is always entitled to lead, based on Quran 8:75, while the Sahibayn place the wali last. Understand the evidence: the incident of Hasan ibn Ali's funeral where Husain put forward the governor as Sunnah.
The tarjih (preferred view) is the order with sultan first.
4
Apply the ruling on repetition (i'adah)
If a non-wali/non-sultan leads, the wali may repeat. If the sultan or someone ahead of wali leads, the wali cannot repeat. If the wali leads, no one may pray after him because the obligation is fulfilled and nafl is not prescribed.
The right of i'adah exists only when the one who led had no entitlement.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i allows multiple janazah prayers on the same deceased. Examine his proofs: the Prophet's prayer at a woman's grave and the Companions' prayers at the Prophet's own funeral before Abu Bakr. Then analyze the Hanafi response: the Prophet's prayer was his exclusive right, and the Companions' prayers occurred before the rightful leader (Abu Bakr) prayed.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that in Hanafi, no repetition is allowed after the rightful leader prays.

باب الجنائز
ہوا تو محلہ کے امام کو آگے بڑھانا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ میت اپنی زندگی میں اس کے امام ہونے پر راضی تھا تو مرنے کے بعد بھی اس کی پسند کا امام بہتر ہے جبکہ شریعت کے مخالف بھی نہیں ہے۔ پھر ولی مستحق امامت ہے اور میت کے اولیاء امامت کے حق میں اسی ترتیب پر ہوں گے جو ترتیب نکاح میں مذکور ہے۔ لیکن نکاح میں عورت کا بیٹا عورت کے باپ پر مقدم ہے۔ اور یہاں باپ اولی بالامامت ہے اور اگر میت کے برابر کے دو ولی ہوں مثلاً اس کے سگے دو بھائی ہوں تو ان میں جس کی عمر زیادہ ہو وہ مقدم ہو گا لیکن اس کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ اپنی جگہ کسی اجنبی کو کر دے مگر یہ کہ دوسرا بھی راضی ہو۔ صاحب عنایہ کے بیان کے مطابق حسن بن زیاد نے ابو حنیفہ سے ترتیب اس طرح نقل کی ہے۔ اول سلطان یعنی خلیفہ پھر جو اس شہر کا سلطان ہے پھر قاضی پھر منتسب حاکم پھر محلہ کا امام پھر ولی میت۔ اس ترتیب کو اکثر مشائخ نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ ترتیب میں ولی کا سب سے آخر میں ہونا طرفین کا قول ہے۔ ورنہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول یہ ہے کہ ولی ہر حال میں میت کی نماز کا مستحق ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے و اولوا الارحام بعضهم اولى ببعض فی کتاب اللہ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حسن بن علی کی جب وفات ہو گئی تو نماز جنازہ کے لئے حسین اور لوگ آئے۔ پس سیدنا حسینؓ نے امامت کے لئے سعید بن العاص کو آگے بڑھایا جو اس زمانہ میں حضرت امیر معاویہ کی طرف سے مدینہ منورہ کے حاکم تھے۔ سعید بن العاص نے آگے بڑھنے سے انکار کیا تو حسین نے ان سے کہا کہ آگے بڑھئے یہی سنت ہے۔ اگر یہ سنت نہ ہوتا تو میں آپ کو آگے نہ بڑھاتا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی پیش کردہ آیت اولو الارحام الآیۃ میراث اور نکاح کی ولایت پر محمول ہے۔ یعنی نکاح کی ولایت صرف اولیاء کو حاصل ہے سلطان وغیرہ کو حاصل نہیں ہے۔ غیر ولی نے نماز جنازہ پڑھائی تو ولی اعادہ کر سکتا ہے
فان صلى غير الولى او السطان اعاد الولى يعنى ان شاء لما ذكرنا ان الحق للاولياء وان صلى الولى لم يجز لاحد ان يصلى بعده لان الفرض يتأدى بالاول والنقل بها غير مشروع ولهذا رأينا الناس تركوا عن آخرهم الصلوة على قبر النبي وهو اليوم كما وضع
ترجمہ .. پس اگر ولی یا سلطان کے علاوہ نے نماز پڑھ دی تو ولی اعادہ کر لے یعنی اگر جی چاہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے کہ حق تو میت کے اولیاء کا ہے۔ اور اگر ولی نے میت پر نماز پڑھی تو اس کے بعد کسی کو میت پر نماز پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ فرض تو پہلے کے پڑھنے سے ادا ہو چکا اور اس نماز کے ساتھ نفل پڑھنا مشروع نہیں ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے ہم نے لوگوں کو دیکھا کہ انہوں نے اول تا آخر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی قبر پر نماز پڑھنا چھوڑ دیا ہے حالانکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم آج بھی ایسے ہی ہیں جیسے (قبر میں ) رکھے گئے تھے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ میت پر اگر ولی اور سلطان کے علاوہ نے نماز پڑھی تو ولی کو نماز جنازہ کے اعادہ کرنے کا حق حاصل ہوگا۔ اور اگر سلطان نے نماز پڑھی یا اس شخص نے پڑھی جو نماز جنازہ کی ترتیب امامت میں ولی پر مقدم ہے تو ولی کو اعادہ کرنے کا حق نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر ولی نے نماز جنازہ پڑھی تو اس کے بعد کسی کو میت پر نماز پڑھنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولی کے نماز پڑھنے سے فرض تو ادا ہو چکا اور نفل اس نماز کے ساتھ مشروع نہیں ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے ولی کے نماز پڑھنے کے بعد کسی کو نماز پڑھنے کا حق نہ ہو گا۔ یہ ہمارا مذہب ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ جنازہ پر مرة بعد مرة نماز کا اعادہ کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک بار حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ایک نئی قبر کے پاس سے گذر ہوا آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کے بارے میں دریافت کیا تو بتلایا گیا کہ فلاں عورت کی قبر ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلمنے فرمایا کہ مجھے نماز کی خبر کیوں نہیں دی تو جواب دیا گیا کہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم اس عورت کو رات میں دفن کیا گیا ہے ہم کو ڈر ہوا کہ حشرات الارض آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو اذیت نہ پہنچا دیں۔ اس لئے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو خبر نہیں دی۔ یہ سن کر آپ نے کھڑے ہو کر اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی۔ نیز رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے جنازہ پر صحابہ کا جوق در جوق آکر نماز پڑھنا ثابت ہے۔ ان دونوں واقعوں سے ایک مرتبہ کے بعد دوسری اور تیسری بار نماز پڑھنے کا ثبوت ملتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل گذر چکی کہ ولی یا سلطان جس نے پہلے نماز پڑھی ہے اسکے پڑھنے سے فرض تو ادا ہو چکا اور نماز جنازہ میں نفل مشروع نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی قبر مبارک پر تمام لوگوں نے نماز پڑھنا ترک کر دیا ہے۔ اور اگر نماز جنازہ میں نفل مشروع ہوتا تو اجتماعی طور پر اس کو ترک نہ کیا جاتا۔ درانحالیکہ رسول اکرم سید الام صلى الله عليه وسلم آج بھی اپنی قبر میں اسی طرح آرام فرما ہیں جس طرح آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو دفن کیا گیا تھا۔ کیونکہ انبیاء کا گوشت زمین پر حرام ہے۔ انبیاء کے جسم کو زمین کی مٹی متغیر نہیں کر سکتی۔ رہا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا اس عورت کی قبر پر نماز پڑھنا تو یہ اس لئے تھا کہ یہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا حق ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے النبى اولى بالمؤمنين من انفسهم آنحضور کے اس حق کو ساقط کرنے کی کسی کو ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے دوسرے واقعہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صدیق اکبر خلیفہ ہونے کی وجہ سے رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز جنازہ کے زیادہ حقدار تھے لیکن آپ معاملات کی درستگی اور فتنہ کو فرو کرنے میں مشغول ہو گئے اور لوگ آپ کی تشریف آوری سے پہلے ہی آکر نماز پڑھنے لگے جب آپ مسئلہ خلافت سے فارغ ہو چکے تو آپ نے نماز پڑھی پھر آپ کے بعد رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے جنازہ پر کسی نے نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔
Chapter of Funerals. It is mustahabb to put forward the imam of the locality because the deceased was pleased with him as imam in his life, so after death his preferred imam is better as long as it does not oppose the Shariah. Then the wali is entitled to lead, and the wali's of the deceased have the same order of entitlement as mentioned in nikah. However, in nikah the son of the woman is preferred over her father, and here the father is more entitled to lead. If there are two equal wali's, e.g., two full brothers, the older is preferred, but he does not have the right to appoint a stranger instead unless the other agrees. According to Sahib al-Inayah, Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa the following order: first the sultan (caliph), then the sultan of that city, then the judge, then the appointed ruler, then the imam of the locality, then the wali of the deceased. Most mashayikh have adopted this order. The wali being last is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). However, Imam Abu Yusuf's view is that the wali is entitled to the prayer of the deceased in all circumstances because Allah says: 'And those of kinship are more entitled to each other in the Book of Allah.' The evidence of the two is that when Hasan ibn Ali passed away, Husain and others came for the funeral prayer. Then Sayyiduna Husain put forward Sa'id ibn al-As to lead, who was the governor of Medina appointed by Amir Muawiyah. Sa'id ibn al-As declined, so Husain told him: 'Go forward, this is the Sunnah. If this were not the Sunnah, I would not put you forward.' The verse presented by Imam Abu Yusuf is interpreted as guardianship for inheritance and marriage, i.e., guardianship for marriage only belongs to wali's, not to the sultan etc. If someone other than the wali or sultan leads the prayer, the wali may repeat, meaning if he wishes, because we mentioned that the right belongs to the wali's. If the wali leads, no one may pray after him because the obligation is discharged by the first, and supererogatory prayer with it is not prescribed. For this reason we saw that people completely abandoned offering prayer at the grave of the Prophet, although he is today as he was placed. Explanation: If someone other than the wali and sultan has led the prayer, the wali has the right to repeat it. If the sultan has led, or the one who is ahead of the wali in the order of imamah, then the wali does not have the right to repeat. And if the wali led, then after that no one is allowed to pray over the deceased. The proof is that with the prayer of the wali, the obligation is fulfilled, and supererogatory prayer with it is not prescribed. Therefore after the wali's prayer, no one has the right to pray. This is our madhhab. Imam Shafi'i said that the funeral prayer can be repeated multiple times. His evidence: once the Prophet passed by a new grave and inquired about it, and was told it was the grave of a certain woman. The Prophet said: 'Why was I not informed about the prayer?' They replied: 'O Messenger of Allah, she was buried at night, and we feared that vermin would harm you.' So the Prophet stood and prayed at her grave. Also, it is proven that the Companions came in groups to pray at the funeral of the Prophet. Both incidents show that prayer can be performed a second and third time. Our evidence has already been given: when the wali or sultan prayed first, the obligation is fulfilled, and supererogatory prayer in funeral prayer is not prescribed. That is why all people have stopped praying at the blessed grave of the Prophet. If supererogatory prayer had been prescribed, they would not have collectively abandoned it. While the Prophet is still in his grave as he was buried, because the flesh of prophets is forbidden to the earth, the earth's soil cannot change their bodies. As for the Prophet's prayer at the grave of that woman, it was because it was his right. Allah says: 'The Prophet is more entitled to the believers than themselves.' No one has the authority to nullify his right. The answer to the second incident is that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, being the caliph, was more entitled to lead the funeral prayer of the Prophet, but he was occupied with settling affairs and quelling strife, and people came and prayed before his arrival. When he finished with the caliphate issue, he prayed, and after him no one prayed at the funeral of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the order of priority for leading funeral prayer and the right to repeat. The author begins with the ruling that it is mustahabb for the local imam to lead if the deceased was pleased with him. Then he states that the wali is entitled, and the order of wali's follows that of guardianship in marriage, with the father preferred over the son here. If there are two equal wali's, the elder leads, but cannot delegate to a stranger without the other's consent. The author then presents a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa listing the order: sultan, city ruler, judge, appointed governor, local imam, then wali. Most mashayikh adopt this. The 'tarfayn' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) place the wali last, but Abu Yusuf holds the wali is always entitled, citing Quran 8:75. The opposing evidence is the incident of Hasan ibn Ali's funeral where Husain put forward the governor Sa'id ibn al-As, and Husain called it Sunnah. Abu Yusuf interprets the verse as referring to inheritance and marriage guardianship. The passage then rules that if a non-wali/non-sultan leads, the wali may repeat; if the sultan or someone ahead of wali leads, the wali cannot repeat; if the wali leads, no one else may pray. This is because the obligation is fulfilled and nafl is not prescribed in janazah. The author cites that people abandoned praying at the Prophet's grave, showing that supererogatory prayer is not allowed. The Shafi'i view allowing multiple prayers is refuted: the Prophet's prayer at the woman's grave was his special right, and the Companions' prayers at his own funeral were before Abu Bakr's prayer; after he prayed, no one else did.

Key Terms
ولی (walī): The guardian or relative entitled to lead funeral prayer, following the order of asabah.
اعادہ (iʿādah): The act of repeating the funeral prayer by the wali if a non-eligible person led it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the wali has already led the funeral prayer, can another person pray the janazah again for the same deceased?
A) Yes, because multiple prayers are recommended.
B) No, because the obligation is fulfilled and nafl is not prescribed in janazah.
C) Yes, but only if the wali permits.
D) No, unless the deceased is a martyr.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi funeral prayer, the sultan takes precedence over the wali; after the wali leads, no repetition is allowed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Funeral Prayer at the Grave: Ruling and Condition of Non-Decomposition
Ruling and condition for salat al-qabr after missing janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-qabr, explain the condition of non-decomposition, and distinguish between the views of Imam Abu Yusuf and the relied-upon view based on predominant opinion.

Core Idea
Salat al-qabr completes the missed janazah wajib, but only before the body decomposes — determined by predominant opinion.

The Prophet prayed at the grave of an Ansari woman to teach us that if the funeral prayer was missed before burial, it can be offered at the grave. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling, the key condition of non-decomposition (yatafassakh), and how the school determines that condition using predominant opinion (ghalabat al-ra'y) rather than a fixed time limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Salat al-janazah at the grave. What is the hukm? Wajib (completion of the missed janazah).
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's action.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the Prophet praying at the grave of an Ansari woman. Type: Sunnah ahad, muttafaq alayh.
The proof is quoted in the text.
3
Identify the condition
The prayer must be offered before the body decomposes (yatafassakh). This is the time limit.
Decomposition is the key barrier.
4
Understand the criterion for decomposition
The relied-upon view uses predominant opinion (ghalabat al-ra'y), not a fixed period. Decay varies with condition, time, and place.
This is the correct view according to the sharh.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf restricts to three days; but the correct view is based on ghalabat al-ra'y because decay varies.
The mufta bihi is the predominant opinion view.

وان دفن الميت ولم يصل عليه على قبره لان النبي صلى على قبر امرأة من الانصار ويصلى عليه قبل ان يتفسخ والمعتبر فى معرفة ذلك اكبر الرأى هو الصحيح لاختلاف الحال والزمان والمكان
ترجمہ .... اور اگر میت اس حال میں دفن کی گئی کہ اس پر نماز نہیں ہوئی تھی تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک انصاری عورت کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی ہے۔ اور قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے میت کے پھول پھٹنے سے پہلے اور اس کی معرفت میں معتبر غالب رائے ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ حال، زمانہ اور مکان مختلف ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ میت اگر بغیر نماز کے دفن ہوگئی تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے دلیل یہ کہ ایک انصاری عورت کو اس حال میں دفن کر دیا گیا تھا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی تھی۔ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کو جب اس کا علم ہوا تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ قبر پر نماز پڑھنے کی اجازت میت کے خراب اور متفرق الاجزاء ہونے سے پہلے پہلے ہے پھول پھٹنے کے بعد اجازت نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ نہ پھول پھٹنے کی شناخت میں غالب رائے معتبر ہے یعنی جب تک غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ نعش پھولی پھٹی نہیں ہے تو قبر پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جاسکتی ہے اور جب پھول پھٹنے کا غالب گمان ہو گیا تو اب یہ اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے کہا ہے کہ تدفین کے بعد تین دن تک قبر پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اسکے بعد جائز نہیں ہے۔ قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے سر نعش کا خراب ہونا میت کے حال کے اختلاف سے مختلف ہوتا رہتا ہے حتی کہ موٹا تازہ بہ نسبت دبلے سوکھے کے جلدی خراب اور ریختہ
And if the deceased is buried and no funeral prayer has been performed over him, then prayer is offered at his grave because the Prophet prayed at the grave of an Ansari woman. And it is prayed before the body decomposes. The criterion for knowing that is predominant opinion, and that is correct due to differences of condition, time, and place. Explanation: If the deceased is buried without prayer, then prayer is offered at the grave. The proof is that an Ansari woman was buried while the Prophet had not prayed over her. When the Prophet learned of it, he prayed at her grave. Sahib al-Quduri said: Permission to pray at the grave is before the body becomes decomposed and disintegrated; after decomposition it is not permitted. Sahib al-Hidayah said: Concerning the knowledge of decomposition, predominant opinion is considered, i.e., as long as there is a strong presumption that the body has not swollen and burst, prayer at the grave can be performed, and when there is a strong presumption of decomposition, then this permission ceases. This is the correct view. Imam Abu Yusuf said: It is permissible to pray at the grave up to three days after burial, after which it is not permissible. The proof of the correct view is that the decay of the body varies according to the condition of the deceased, so that a fat, fresh body decays quickly compared to a thin, dry one.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses the ruling of salat al-janazah 'ala al-qabr (funeral prayer at the grave) for someone who was buried without the funeral prayer being performed. The author states the ruling: if a deceased is buried without janazah, prayer is performed at the grave. The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet praying at the grave of an Ansari woman. The condition is that the prayer must be offered before the body decomposes (yatafassakh). The text discusses the criterion for determining decomposition: predominant opinion (ghalabat al-ra'y) is used, as it varies with climate, time, and place. Sahib al-Quduri restricts permission to before physical decomposition. Sahib al-Hidayah emphasizes predominant opinion: as long as one strongly thinks the body has not decayed, prayer is allowed. Imam Abu Yusuf gives a fixed period of three days after burial. The correct view (as per the sharh) is the one based on predominant opinion, because decay depends on the condition of the body (fat vs. thin, etc.). The passage ends with a note that a fat fresh body decays faster than a thin dry one.

Key Terms
یتفسخ (yatafassakh): The decomposition or disintegration of the body after burial (bloating, bursting).
غالب الرأی (ghālib al-ra'y): Predominant opinion or strong presumption; the criterion for judging if the body has decomposed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the time limit for offering funeral prayer at the grave of a person buried without janazah?
A) Exactly three days after burial.
B) Before the body decomposes, determined by predominant opinion.
C) Up to one month after burial.
D) It can be done at any time, even after decomposition.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-qabr is wajib before decomposition, determined by predominant opinion, not a fixed time period.

Grave Prayer for the Deceased Buried Without Janazah
Ruling with evidence and intra-Hanafi dispute on grave prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for performing Janazah prayer at the grave according to the Hanafi school and explain why predominant opinion (ghalib al-rai) is used instead of a fixed time.

Core Idea
A funeral prayer at the grave is permitted before the body decomposes, determined by predominant opinion, not a fixed period.

This lesson examines a well-known Hanafi ruling: when a deceased Muslim is buried without the Janazah prayer, the prayer may still be offered at the grave. The evidence comes from the Prophet's own action. However, the permission is conditional — the body must not have decomposed. The key question is how to determine decomposition. The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, relies on the predominant opinion of those present, rather than a fixed number of days. This flexible approach accounts for variations in climate, soil, and the condition of the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the performance of Janazah prayer at the grave of a deceased who was buried without the prayer. The ruling is that it is permitted (recommended) before the body decomposes.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence is the Prophet's (s.a.w) action: he prayed at the grave of an Ansari woman who had been buried without Janazah. This indicates permissibility and recommendation.
Hadith from Sahih Muslim
3
Analyze the condition (shart)
The prayer is only valid if the body has not decomposed (tafasukh). Determine how to know this: the Hanafi school uses predominant opinion (ghalib al-rai), not a fixed time.
Factors like season, climate, and body condition affect decomposition.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf limited the permission to three days after burial. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani rely on predominant opinion. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the latter, as stated in al-Hidayah.
Tarjih by al-Marghinani
5
Evaluate the response to the objection
The objection: the Prophet prayed at the graves of Uhud martyrs after eight years. Hanafi scholars answer either that it was a supplication (dua) interpreted as 'prayer', or that martyrs' bodies also decay, so the same condition applies.

وان دفن الميت ولم يصل عليه على قبره لان النبي صلى على قبر امرأة من الانصار ويصلى عليه قبل ان يتفسخ والمعتبر فى معرفة ذلك اكبر الرأى هو الصحيح لاختلاف الحال والزمان والمكان ترجمہ .... اور اگر میت اس حال میں دفن کی گئی کہ اس پر نماز نہیں ہوئی تھی تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک انصاری عورت کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی ہے۔ اور قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے میت کے پھول پھٹنے سے پہلے اور اس کی معرفت میں معتبر غالب رائے ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ حال، زمانہ اور مکان مختلف ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ میت اگر بغیر نماز کے دفن ہوگئی تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی جائے دلیل یہ کہ ایک انصاری عورت کو اس حال میں دفن کر دیا گیا تھا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی تھی ۔ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کو جب اس کا علم ہوا تو اس کی قبر پر نماز پڑھی۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ قبر پر نماز پڑھنے کی اجازت میت کے خراب اور متفرق الاجزاء ہونے سے پہلے پہلے ہے پھول پھٹنے کے بعد اجازت نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ نہ پھول پھٹنے کی شناخت میں غالب رائے معتبر ہے یعنی جب تک غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ نعش پھولی پھٹی نہیں ہے تو قبر پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جاسکتی ہے اور جب پھول پھٹنے کا غالب گمان ہو گیا تو اب یہ اجازت نہ ہوگی ۔ یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے کہا ہے کہ تدفین کے بعد تین دن تک قبر پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اسکے بعد جائز نہیں ہے۔ قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے سر نعش کا خراب ہونا میت کے حال کے اختلاف سے مختلف ہوتا رہتا ہے حتی کہ موٹا تازہ بہ نسبت دبلے سوکھے کے جلدی خراب اور ریختہ ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح موسم اور مکان کے اختلاف سے مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ حتی کہ گرمی اور برسات کے موسم میں یہ نسبت سردی کے موسم میں. جلدی سڑ جاتا ہے اور سیلی اور نمناک زمین میں یہ نسبت خشک زمین کے جلدی خراب ہو جاتا ہے۔ بہر حال جب غالب گمان معتبر ہے تو اگر غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ تین دن سے پہلے ہی نعش گل سڑ گئی ہوگی۔ تو اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے گی اور اگر غالب گمان یہ ہو کہ تین دن کے بعد بھی خراب نہیں ہوتی ہے تو اس پر تین دن کے بعد بھی نماز پڑھنے کی اجازت ہے۔ رہا یہ کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے آٹھ سال بعد شہداء احد پر نماز پڑھی ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے شہداء احد کے لئے دعا کی ہے جس کو لفظ صلی کے ساتھ تعبیر کر دیا گیا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ شہداء کے اجسام بھی چونکہ گلتے سڑتے ہیں ہیں اس لئے ان کی قبروں پر نماز پڑھنے میں کیا مضائقہ ہے۔
Ruling on performing Janazah prayer at the grave for one who was buried without the prayer: If a deceased is buried and no funeral prayer has been performed over him, then prayer is performed at his grave because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed at the grave of a woman from the Ansar. And the prayer is offered before the body decomposes. The criterion for knowing that is predominant opinion, and this is the correct view because circumstances, times, and places differ. Explanation: The issue is that if a deceased is buried without prayer, then prayer is performed at his grave. The evidence is that an Ansari woman was buried without the Prophet (peace be upon him) having performed the funeral prayer over her. When the Prophet (peace be upon him) learned of this, he prayed at her grave. Imam al-Quduri said that the permission to pray at the grave is before the body decays and its parts disintegrate; after decomposition there is no permission. The author of al-Hidayah said that in determining the condition of decomposition, predominant opinion is relied upon: as long as one's dominant belief is that the corpse has not swollen or burst, then the funeral prayer may be performed at the grave; when the dominant belief is that it has decomposed, then this permission ceases. This is the correct saying. Imam Abu Yusuf said that it is permissible to pray at the grave for three days after burial, after which it is not permissible. The evidence for the correct saying is that the decomposition of the corpse varies with differences in the condition of the deceased, even that a fat and fresh body decomposes faster than a lean and dry one. Similarly, it varies with differences in season and place, even that in hot and rainy seasons it rots faster than in cold seasons, and in wet and damp ground it decays faster than in dry ground. Nevertheless, when predominant opinion is considered valid, if the dominant belief is that the corpse has decomposed before three days, then prayer will not be performed; if the dominant belief is that it has not decomposed even after three days, then prayer is allowed even after three days. As for the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed over the martyrs of Uhud after eight years, the answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made supplication (dua) for them, which was expressed with the word 'prayed' (salla). Another answer is that the bodies of martyrs also decay, so there is no harm in praying at their graves.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence on performing Janazah prayer at the grave when the deceased was buried without it. The Hanafi position, based on the Prophet's (s.a.w) action of praying at an Ansari woman's grave, permits this prayer before the body decomposes. The key condition is that the body has not yet decomposed (tafasukh). The criterion for determining this is the predominant opinion (ghalib al-rai) of those present, not a fixed time frame. This is the correct view (sahih qawl) according to al-Hidayah. In contrast, Imam Abu Yusuf restricted the period to three days, but the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely on the varying factors affecting decomposition: season, climate, soil, and the condition of the deceased's body. Therefore, if one's dominant belief is that the body has decomposed within three days, the prayer is not performed; if it is believed intact after three days, it may still be performed. The passage also addresses an objection: the Prophet prayed at the graves of Uhud martyrs after eight years. The Hanafi response is that this was a supplication (dua) interpreted as prayer, or that martyrs' bodies also decay, thus the general ruling applies. Overall, the ruling is that praying at the grave is a recommended sunnah, but it is not obligatory since the original funeral prayer had already been performed by some.

Key Terms
غالب الرأي (ghalib al-rai): Predominant opinion; the strongest probable belief based on available evidence, used to determine whether the body has decomposed.
تفسخ (tafasukh): Decomposition of the body; the process of decay and disintegration.
قبر (qabr): Grave; the burial place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The predominant opinion (ghalib al-rai) of those present.

D) The opinion of the deceased's family.

Key Takeaway
The Janazah prayer at the grave is permissible before decomposition, assessed by predominant opinion, not a set number of days.

Method of Janazah Prayer: Four Takbirs and the Latecomer Rule
Description of the proper method of performing Janazah prayer including takbirs and supplications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proper method of performing Janazah prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the rule for the latecomer (masbuq) based on the evidence of the Prophet's last practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet's last Janazah had four takbirs, fixing the number and making the latecomer wait for the next takbir.

Janazah prayer has a unique structure distinct from regular salah. The Hanafi school bases this structure on the final practice of the Prophet (s.a.w). In this lesson, we explore the four takbirs, the recitations after each, and the controversial rule for those who join late. Understanding the proof (dalil) will clarify why the school insists on four takbirs and how the latecomer should act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The Janazah prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). Its method, including the four takbirs and specific recitations, is the established sunnah based on the Prophet's action.
The four takbirs are considered essential (fard) for the prayer; the recitations after each are sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the Prophet's last Janazah prayer in which he performed four takbirs. This action abrogates any earlier practice with more or fewer takbirs.
The Hadith is narrated in Sahih Muslim, Kitab al-Jana'iz.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the later action (fi'li) of the Prophet abrogates earlier ones. Since the last Janazah had exactly four takbirs, the number is fixed at four. The recitations after each takbir are derived from other narrations.
The Prophet's consistent practice establishes the sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar allowed the Imam to add a fifth takbir, but the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rejected this as abrogated. For the latecomer (masbuq), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule that he does not say any takbir until the Imam says another after his arrival; Abu Yusuf holds he says the missed takbir immediately.
The dispute on the latecomer is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mukhtar) position is the four-takbir method and the latecomer waiting for the next takbir, as per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah affirms this as the chosen view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز پڑھنے کا طریقہ

والصلوة ان يكبر تكبيرة يحمد الله عقيبها ثم يكبر تكبيرة ويصلى على النبي ثم يكبر تكبيرة يدعو فيها لنفسه وللميت وللمسلمين ثم يكبر الرابعة ويسلم لانه اكبر اربعا في أخر صلواة صلاها فنسخت ما قبلها ولوكبر الامام خمسا لم يتابعه الموتم خلافا لزفر لانه منسوخ لما روينا وينتظر تسليمة الامام في رواية وهو المختار والاتيان بالدعوات استغفار للميت والبداية بالثناء ثم بالصلوة سنة الدعاء ولا يستغفر للصبى ولكن يقول اللهم اجعله لنا فرطا واجعله لنا اجر او ذخرا واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا ولو كبر الامام تكبيرة او تكبيرتين لا يكبر الاتى حتى يكبر اخرى بعد حضوره عند ابي حنيفة و محمد و قال ابويوسف يكبر حين يحضر لان الاولى للافتتاح والمسبوق ياتى به ولهما ان كل تكبير قائمة مقام ركعة والمسبوق لا يبتدى بما فاته اذهو منسوخ ولوكان حاضرا فلم يكبر مع الامام لايننظر الثانية بالاتفاق لانه بمنزلة المدرك

ترجمہ اور نماز جنازہ کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ تکبیر کہے اسی تکبیر کے بعد اللہ کی ثناء کرے پھر تکبیر کہے۔ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود بھیجے پھر تکبیر کہے اس میں دعا کرے اپنے واسطے، میت کے واسطے اور تمام مسلمانوں کے واسطے پھر چوتھی تکبیر کہے اور سلام پھیر دے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جو سب سے آخر میں نماز جنازہ پڑھی اس میں چارہی تکبیرات کہیں۔ تو اس نے سابق کو منسوخ کر دیا ہے۔ اور اگر امام نے پانچ تکبیرات کہیں تو مقتدی ( چار سے زائد میں ) اس کی پیروی نہ کرے گا ۔ امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ مار دینا کی وجہ سے چار سے زائد منسوخ ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں امام کے سلام پھیرنے کا انتظار کرے۔ یہی مختار ہے اور دعائیں کرنا میت کے لئے مغفرت مانگنا ہوتا ہے اور ثناء کے ساتھ شروع کرنا پھر درود کے ساتھ دعا کی سنت ہے ۔ اور بچہ کے لئے استغفار نہ کرے۔ لیکن یوں کہے ( الہی اس بچہ کو ہمارے واسطے فارط کر دے اور اس کو ہمارے لیئے ثواب اور ذخیرہ نیکی کر دے اور اس کو ہمارے لئے ایسا شفاعت کرنے والا کر دے جس کی شفاعت قبول ہو۔ اور اگر امام ایک یا دو تکبیریں کہہ چکا تو آنے والا تکبیر نہ کہے یہاں تک کہ امام اس کے آنے کے بعد تکبیر کہے ۔ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ حاضر ہوتے ہی چھوٹی ہوئی تکبیر میں کہہ لے۔ کیونکہ پہلی تکبیر افتتاح کے واسطے ہے اور مسبوق اس کو ضرور لاتا ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہر تکبیر ایک رکعت کے قائم مقام ہے اور مسبوق اس نماز کو ادا کرنا شروع نہیں کرتا جو اس سے چھوٹ گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ منسوخ ہو گیا ہے۔
Method of prayer: The prayer is that he says a takbir, and after it praises Allah, then says a takbir and sends blessings upon the Prophet, then says a takbir and makes supplication in it for himself, for the deceased, and for the Muslims, then says the fourth takbir and makes salutations. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said four takbirs in the last prayer he performed, so it abrogated what came before. If the Imam says five takbirs, the follower should not follow him in that, contrary to Zufar, because it is abrogated as we narrated. And he waits for the Imam's salutation in one narration, and that is the chosen view. And performing the supplications is seeking forgiveness for the deceased, and beginning with praise and then with blessings is the sunnah of supplication. He does not seek forgiveness for a child, but says: 'O Allah, make him for us a forerunner, and make him for us a reward and a treasure, and make him for us an intercessor and accepted intercessor.' If the Imam has said one or two takbirs, the newcomer does not say takbir until the Imam says another after his arrival, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said that he says takbir when he arrives because the first takbir is for opening and the one who missed it brings it. The argument of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that every takbir stands in the position of a rak'ah, and the one who missed does not begin with what he missed because it has been abrogated. If a person is present and did not say takbir with the Imam, he does not wait for the second by agreement because he is like one who perceives (the prayer).
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage details the method (tariqa) of performing Janazah prayer. The Hanafi school prescribes four takbirs (not more, not less), with specific recitations after each. After the first takbir: praising Allah (thana). After the second: sending salawat upon the Prophet. After the third: making supplication (dua) for the deceased, oneself, and all Muslims. After the fourth: saying taslim (salutation). The evidence is the Prophet's (s.a.w) last Janazah prayer, which consisted of four takbirs, abrogating any earlier practice with more or fewer. Therefore, if an Imam says five takbirs, the follower should not join in the extra, according to the majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad); Imam Zufar disagreed, but his view is considered abrogated. The passage also discusses the latecomer (masbuq): if someone arrives after the Imam has already said one or two takbirs, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he should not say any takbir until the Imam says another after his arrival, because each takbir is likened to a rak'ah in regular prayer, and a latecomer does not begin with what he missed. Abu Yusuf held that he should say the missed takbir immediately, but the relied-upon (mukhtar) view is the former. For a deceased child, instead of asking forgiveness (istighfar), one makes a specific supplication, as the child is sinless. This method is the authoritative practice of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تكبيرة (takbirah): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' in the Janazah prayer; each occurrence is considered a pillar (rukn) of the prayer.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the Janazah prayer after the Imam has begun, missing one or more takbirs.
فرط (farat): A forerunner; used in the supplication for a deceased child, meaning the child becomes a means of reward and intercession for the parents in the Hereafter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a latecomer (masbuq) do if he arrives after the Imam has said one takbir in Janazah prayer?
A) Say the missed takbir immediately.
B) Wait for the Imam's next takbir.
C) Leave the prayer and pray alone.
D) Join without saying any takbir until the end.

Key Takeaway
The Janazah prayer consists of four takbirs based on the Prophet's last practice; the latecomer waits for the next takbir because each takbir is like a rak'ah.

Method of Funeral Prayer (Ṣalāt al-Janāzah)
Describes the four takbirs and supplications in funeral prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of the four takbirs in the Hanafi funeral prayer, explain the proof from the Prophet's last prayer, and apply the correct supplication for a deceased child.

Core Idea
Four takbirs: praising, salawat, du'a, salam — the Prophet's last funeral prayer abrogated all other forms.

This lesson covers the way to perform the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school. You will learn the exact order of the four takbirs and what to say after each. We also discuss the evidence from the Prophet's final practice and the special prayer for a child, which omits seeking forgiveness because children have no sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Funeral prayer (ṣalāt al-janāzah) is a communal obligation (fard kifāyah). The passage describes its inner structure: four takbirs with specific recitations. Understand that these are considered wājib in the Hanafi school; omission of any before salām requires repetition.
Distinguish fard from wājib: here the prayer itself is fard, but the specific actions (e.g., four takbirs) are wājib.
2
Locate the dalīl
The proof given is that the Prophet ﷺ performed four takbirs in his last funeral prayer, which abrogated earlier practices with different numbers. This is a sunnah action (fiʿl) serving as evidence.
The text says: 'because he said four takbirs in the last prayer he prayed, so it abrogated what was before it.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The Prophet's consistent final practice (the last funeral prayer he led) demonstrates the ruling. Since his actions are authoritative, the four-takbir format becomes binding. Any earlier variant (e.g., five takbirs) is superseded.
This relies on the principle that the later action abrogates (naskh) earlier ones.
4
Apply the sequence
After each takbir: 1st — praise (thana); 2nd — salawat; 3rd — du'a (for self, deceased, Muslims); 4th — salam. Memorize this order for practice.
No recitation of al-Fātiḥa; the funeral prayer has only one standing (qiyām) and no rukūʿ or sujūd.
5
Note the exception for children
For a deceased child, one does not seek forgiveness (istighfār) because the child has no sins. Instead, the specific du'a is recited: 'O Allah, make him a forerunner (farṭ) and a reward and a treasure, and an intercessor whose intercession is accepted.'
The term 'farṭ' refers to a child who precedes parents to Paradise to intercede for them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلوة ان يكبر تكبيرة يحمد الله عقيبها ثم يكبر تكبيرة ويصلى على النبي ثم يكبر تكبيرة يدعو فيها لنفسه وللميت وللمسلمين ثم يكبر الرابعة ويسلم لانه اكبر اربعا في أخر صلواة صلاها فنسخت ما قبلها ولا يستغفر للصبى ولكن يقول اللهم اجعله لنا فرطا واجعله لنا اجر او ذخرا واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا
And the prayer is that he says takbir, then praises Allah after it, then says takbir and sends salawat upon the Prophet, then says takbir and makes supplication in it for himself, for the deceased, and for the Muslims, then says the fourth takbir and says salam because he said four takbirs in the last prayer he prayed, so it abrogated what was before it. And one does not seek forgiveness for a child, but rather says: O Allah, make him for us a forerunner, and make him for us a reward and a treasure, and make him for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement describing the method of funeral prayer (ṣalāt al-janāzah) in the Hanafi school. The prayer consists of four takbirs. After the first takbir, one praises Allah (thanā). After the second, one sends salawāt upon the Prophet ﷺ. After the third, one makes duʿā for oneself, the deceased, and all Muslims. After the fourth, one says salām. The proof is that the Prophet ﷺ performed four takbirs in his last funeral prayer, abrogating any previous practice with more or fewer. For a deceased child, one does not seek forgiveness (istighfār) because the child has no sins. Instead, one prays for the child to be a forerunner (farṭ) and a stored reward for the parents, and an intercessor.

Key Terms
تكبيرة (takbīra): Each utterance of 'Allāhu Akbar' in the funeral prayer; there are four takbīras.
فرط (faraṭ): A forerunner; a child who precedes his parents to Paradise to intercede for them.

D) Four takbīrs; after the third, one says salām.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi funeral prayer consists of four takbirs with specific supplications after each, based on the Prophet's last prayer which abrogated prior practices, and for a child, istighfār is replaced by a special duʿā making the child a farṭ.

Ruling on Imam Making Five Takbirs
States that followers do not follow the imam in a fifth takbir and should wait for his salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on following an imam who says a fifth takbir in funeral prayer and state the preferred view for the follower's action.

Core Idea
A follower must not follow an imam in an abrogated act; the fifth takbir is mansukh, so the follower waits for the salam.

This lesson addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: what should a follower do when the imam says a fifth takbir in funeral prayer? Imam Zufar held that the follower should follow, but the majority Hanafi position is that the fifth takbir is abrogated. The author clarifies the correct action and the preferred narration regarding waiting for salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the contested action? The follower following the imam in a fifth takbir.
2
State the opposing view
Imam Zufar's argument: Companions did five, so follow.
3
State the Hanafi counter-argument
The fifth takbir is mansukh by the Prophet's final practice of four.
4
Understand the difference among Hanafis
Two narrations on what the follower does: say salam immediately or wait.
5
Know the preferred view
The author chooses waiting for salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوكبر الامام خمسا لم يتابعه الموتم خلافا لزفر لانه منسوخ لما روينا وينتظر تسليمة الامام في رواية وهو المختار
And if the imam says five takbirs, the follower should not follow him, contrary to Zufar, because it is abrogated by what we narrated. And he waits for the imam's salam in one narration, and that is the chosen view.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a follower should follow an imam who performs five takbirs in funeral prayer. Imam Zufar holds that the follower should follow because some Companions (e.g., Ali رضي الله عنه) did five. The dominant Hanafi view is that the fifth takbir is abrogated (mansukh) by the Prophet's last practice of four. Therefore, the follower should NOT say the fifth takbir with the imam. There are two narrations about what the follower should do: either say salam immediately (breaking off) or wait for the imam's salam. The author (al-Marghinani) declares the latter (waiting) as the preferred (mukhtār) view, so that the follower maintains some connection with the imam through salam.

Key Terms
منسوخ (mansūkh): Abrogated; the ruling of five takbirs was abrogated by the Prophet's later action of four.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Say the fifth takbir with him.
B) Remain silent and then say salam immediately.
C) Wait for the imam's salam and then give salam.
D) Leave the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The follower must not follow an imam in a fifth takbir because it is abrogated; instead, he should wait for the imam's salam.

Latecomer (Masbuq) in Funeral Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on masbuq's takbirs in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a masbuq in funeral prayer when he misses one or two takbirs, and explain the intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, each takbir is like a rak'ah; the masbuq waits for the imam's next takbir to join.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). Unlike regular prayer, the funeral prayer consists only of takbirs with no ruku or sujud. When a person arrives late, the question arises: should he begin his takbirs immediately or wait? The answer reveals how Hanafi imams analogize between funeral and regular prayer.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the Scenario
Determine the situation: the imam has already said one or two takbirs of the funeral prayer, and a latecomer arrives. What should the latecomer do?
2
2. State the Dominant Hanafi View
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the latecomer should not say takbir immediately; he should wait until the imam says the next takbir after his arrival. Then he joins and completes missed takbirs after the imam's salam.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.
3
3. State Abu Yusuf's Opposing View
Abu Yusuf argues that the latecomer should say takbir immediately upon joining because the first takbir of any prayer is an opening (iftitah) takbir, which the masbuq must perform upon joining.
He analogizes to regular prayer where the masbuq says the opening takbir immediately.
4
4. Analyze the Hanafi Response
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that each takbir in funeral prayer stands in the place of a rak'ah. Just as a masbuq in regular prayer does not start with a missed rak'ah immediately, here he does not start with missed takbirs. The rule of abrogation (naskh) supports this.
The analogy is based on the similarity of each takbir to a rak'ah in terms of being a unit.
5
5. Determine the Practical Consequence
The difference impacts the sequence: if Abu Yusuf's view is followed, the latecomer would say his first takbir while the imam is on his second, potentially disconnecting the prayer sequence. The relied-upon view avoids this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كبر الامام تكبيرة او تكبيرتين لا يكبر الاتى حتى يكبر اخرى بعد حضوره عند ابي حنيفة و محمد و قال ابويوسف يكبر حين يحضر لان الاولى للافتتاح والمسبوق ياتى به ولهما ان كل تكبير قائمة مقام ركعة والمسبوق لا يبتدى بما فاته اذهو منسوخ
And if the imam has said one or two takbirs, the one arriving should not say takbir until the imam says another after his arrival according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: He says takbir when he arrives because the first takbir is for opening (iftitah) and the masbuq performs it. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), every takbir stands in the place of a rak'ah, and the masbuq does not begin with what he missed because it is abrogated.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a person who arrives late to funeral prayer after the imam has already said one or two takbirs. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the latecomer should NOT start with his missed takbirs immediately; instead, he should wait until the imam says the next takbir (after his arrival) and then join. Their reasoning: each takbir in funeral prayer stands in the place of a rak'ah in regular prayer. Just as a latecomer to regular prayer joins the imam and then makes up missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam, similarly here, the latecomer should wait and then make up the missed takbirs after the imam completes. They argue that beginning with the missed takbir immediately is abrogated. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he says the latecomer should say takbir upon arrival because the first takbir is the iftitah (opening), which the masbuq must perform. He analogizes to regular prayer where the masbuq says the opening takbir upon joining. The text states that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the congregational prayer after the imam has already begun; specifically here, one who missed some takbirs of funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon arriving.
B) After the imam says the third takbir.
C) After the imam finishes all takbirs and before salam.
D) He should not pray and must wait for another congregation.

Key Takeaway
In funeral prayer, the masbuq does not begin with missed takbirs immediately; he waits for the imam's next takbir and completes the missing ones after the imam's salam.

Recitation of Fatiha in Funeral Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Argues against reciting Surah al-Fatiha in funeral prayer, citing hadith and qiyas with sajdah tilawah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on recitation in funeral prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using dalil and qiyas.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is a supplication, not a recitation; its qiyam is for du'a, not for Quran.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding recitation of Surah al-Fatiha in the funeral prayer. While many assume that all prayers with standing require Fatiha, the Hanafi school argues that funeral prayer is a unique form of worship. We will explore the textual evidence from Ibn Umar and the rational analogy with sajdah tilawah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on recitation in funeral prayer: no Quranic recitation, only glorification and salawāt.
The Hanafi view is that the qiyam is for du'a, not recitation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i considers recitation of al-Fatiha obligatory in funeral prayer, analogizing it to regular prayers with qiyam.
Shafi'i view: funeral prayer is a prayer like any other with standing.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i qiyas: funeral prayer has qiyam, so it requires Fatiha as in other prayers.
The basis is the general principle that every prayer with standing requires recitation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: funeral prayer is unique; its single qiyam is for supplication, not recitation. Analogy with sajdah tilawah, where recitation is not done.
The Hanafi also rely on the hadith of Ibn Umar that he did not recite in funeral prayer.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: for Shafi'is, missing Fatiha invalidates the prayer; for Hanafis, the prayer is valid without it.
This affects how an imam leads in mixed congregations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان ابن عمر كان لا يقرأ في الصلوة على الجنازة
Ibn Umar used not to recite (Quran) in the funeral prayer.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha in funeral prayer. Imam Shafi’i considers recitation of al-Fatiha obligatory in funeral prayer, analogizing it to other prayers with qiyam (standing). The Hanafi school refutes this with two arguments: (1) A hadith from Ibn Umar that he did not recite Quran in funeral prayer. (2) A rational argument (qiyas) that funeral prayer consists of only one pillar (qiyam) with supplications; it is like sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation), where Quran recitation is not prescribed because it is a single act of worship. Therefore, recitation is not part of funeral prayer. The Hanafi position is that one does not recite al-Fatiha; instead, after the first takbir, one praises Allah (thanā) and sends salawāt.

Key Terms
قراءة (qirā’a): Recitation of Quran, specifically al-Fatiha, in funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Surah al-Fatiha not recited in funeral prayer?
A) Because the Prophet never recited it in any prayer.
B) Because funeral prayer has only one standing (qiyam) and is like sajdah tilawah.
C) Because it is a supplication prayer, not a recitation prayer.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, funeral prayer does not require recitation of Quran; it is a prayer of supplication, analogous to sajdah tilawah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Funeral Prayer: Four Takbirs and No Fatiha Recitation
Explains the four takbirs and actions, with the Hanafi view on no Fatiha recitation and the dispute with Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions after each takbir in Hanafi funeral prayer and explain the Hanafi proof for not reciting Fatiha.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer has only standing; Fatiha is not prescribed, unlike other prayers.

Funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) with a unique structure. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi view that it consists of four takbirs with specific actions after each, and we analyze the proof that recitation of Surah al-Fatiha is not part of it. This distinction sets the Hanafi school apart from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Structure
Funeral prayer is defined as four takbirs. After the opening takbir (takbir al-iftitah), the worshipper praises Allah (thanā). After the second takbir, blessings (durud) are sent upon the Prophet. After the third takbir, supplication (dua) is made for self, deceased, and all Muslims. After the fourth takbir, salam is given.
This sequence is specific to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the Hanafi Proof (Dalil)
The Hanafi proof against reciting Fatiha is the narration from Nafi' that Ibn Umar did not recite in funeral prayer. Additionally, a rational proof (dalil aqli) is that funeral prayer has only one pillar (standing), and just as in sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation), recitation is not prescribed in a single pillar.
The naqli proof is a companion practice (qawl sahabi), which is weaker than mutawatir but used here.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i Counter-Argument
Imam Shafi'i analogizes (qiyas) funeral prayer to other prayers, arguing that recitation is required in all prayers. The Hanafi response uses the specific practice of Ibn Umar to block this qiyas, and the rational proof shows the distinction of a single-pillar prayer.
This is a classic ikhtilaf between dalil naqli (specific) and qiyas (general).
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that no Fatiha is recited, and after the fourth takbir, no supplication is made before salam (according to Zahir al-Riwayah).
Some later scholars recommend dua after fourth takbir, but the mufta bihi is to follow Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text

اراد احدكم ان يدعو فليحمد الله وليصل على النبي ثم يدعو یعنی جب تم میں سے کوئی دعا کا ارادہ کرے تو اللہ کی حمد کرے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھے پھر دعا پڑھے۔ پھر چوتھی تکبیر کہہ کر سلام پھیر دے، چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد سلام پھیرنا اس لئے ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سب سے آخری نماز جنازہ میں چار ہی تکبیرات کہی ہیں۔ پس اس سے پہلے کا عمل اگر اس کے مخالف بھی ہو تو وہ منسوخ ہو گیا ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ چوتھی تکبیر کے بعد اور سلام سے پہلے ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق کوئی دعا نہیں ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ سلام سے پہلے یہ دعا پڑھے ربنا آتنا فی الدنيا حسنة وفي الآخرة حسنة وقنا برحمتك عذاب القبر و عذاب النار اور بعض نے فرمایا کہ یہ کہے ربنا لا تزع قلوبنا بعد اذ هديتنا وهب لنا من لدنک رحمة انك انت الوهاب
Chapter of Funerals. The explanation: This passage describes the manner of funeral prayer. Thus it says: Funeral prayer is the name of four takbirs. The detail is that after intention, he says the opening takbir and raises both hands to the ears; after that he praises Allah, i.e. says 'Alhamdulillah' and similar words, and some have said he says 'Subhanakallahumma wabihamdika' etc., as in other prayers. According to us, recitation of Surah al-Fatiha after the first takbir is not prescribed. Imam Shafi'i holds the opinion of reciting Fatiha. Imam Shafi'i analogizes funeral prayer to other prayers. So just as in other prayers recitation of Quran is necessary, similarly in funeral prayer recitation is necessary. Our proof is that it is narrated from Nafi' that Ibn Umar did not recite in funeral prayer. The rational proof is that funeral prayer is only the name of one pillar (standing), and in a single pillar, recitation of Quran is not prescribed. Just as in prostration of recitation, because it is a single pillar, recitation is not prescribed. Then he says the second takbir and sends blessings (durud) upon the Messenger of Allah, because after praising Allah, sending blessings upon the Prophet is appropriate, as is the order in Tashahhud, and sermons are structured on this order. Then he says the third takbir and prays for himself, the deceased, and all Muslims. If he remembers, he recites the supplication 'Allahummaghfir li hayyina wa mayyitina' etc., and if he does not remember, he recites whatever supplication he knows. Supplication is placed after praise and blessings because the Prophet said: 'When any of you intends to supplicate, let him praise Allah and send blessings upon the Prophet, then supplicate.' Then he says the fourth takbir and makes salam. He makes salam after the fourth takbir because the Prophet said only four takbirs in the last funeral prayer. So the previous practice, even if contrary, is abrogated. The author of al-‘Inayah wrote that after the fourth takbir and before salam, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, there is no supplication. And some mashayikh said that before salam he should recite: 'Rabbana atina fid-dunya hasanah wa fil-akhirati hasanah waqina birahmatika ‘adhab al-qabri wa ‘adhab an-nar.' And some said he should say: 'Rabbana la tuzigh qulubana ba’da idh hadaytana wahablana min ladunka rahmah innaka anta al-wahhab.'
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This is a commentary passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explaining the description of funeral prayer as stated in al-Hidayah. The author begins by stating that funeral prayer consists of four takbirs. After the intention and opening takbir, one raises hands and then praises Allah. The Hanafi position is that recitation of Surah al-Fatiha is not prescribed after the first takbir, unlike the Shafi'i school which analogizes funeral prayer to other prayers. The Hanafi proof is from the practice of Ibn Umar (narration from Nafi') and a rational analogy: funeral prayer has only one pillar (standing), and in isolated pillars like sajdah tilawah, recitation is not prescribed. After the second takbir, one sends blessings on the Prophet, following the order in Tashahhud. After the third takbir, one supplicates for all, and the Prophet's instruction to begin supplication with praise and blessings is cited. After the fourth takbir, one makes salam. The author notes that according to Zahir al-Riwayah, no supplication is made between the fourth takbir and salam, though some later scholars recommend specific duas.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' in prayer; in funeral prayer, four takbirs are performed.
تکبیر افتتاح (takbir al-iftitah): The first takbir with which prayer begins, accompanied by raising hands.
قرأت (qira'ah): Recitation of Quranic verses in prayer; in funeral prayer, the Hanafi view is that it is not prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what action follows the second takbir in funeral prayer?
A) Supplication
B) Praise of Allah
C) Blessings on the Prophet
D) Salam

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer consists of four takbirs with specific actions; the Hanafi school does not prescribe Quranic recitation, supported by companion practice and rational analogy.

The Fifth Takbir in Funeral Prayer: Follower's Duty
Discusses the ruling when an imam says a fifth takbir and the follower's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling when an imam says a fifth takbir in funeral prayer and state the relied-upon (mukhtar) action for the follower.

Core Idea
A fifth takbir is abrogated; the follower must not follow, but should wait for the imam's salam.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about what a follower should do if the imam adds a fifth takbir in the funeral prayer. The majority position, supported by the final practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), holds that the fifth takbir is abrogated. However, Imam Zufar and some Companions' practice suggest following. The passage resolves the conflict and provides two narrations from Abu Hanifa, with the author of al-Hidayah choosing the view that the follower should wait for the imam's salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize that the core question is whether the follower should follow the imam's extra takbir in funeral prayer.
2
State the Al-Quduri Position
Al-Quduri holds that the follower should not follow because the fifth takbir is abrogated; only four takbirs are valid.
The abrogation is based on the Prophet's final practice.
3
State Imam Zufar's Position and His Proof
Imam Zufar argues that the follower should follow because the matter is disputed, citing the narration of Ali saying five takbirs.
His proof is a Companion practice.
4
Trace the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response is that the Companions ultimately referred to the Prophet's last funeral prayer, which had four takbirs, thus abrogating the fifth. Therefore, following the extra takbir is erroneous.
This response uses the principle of abrogation (naskh) based on later practice.
5
Determine the Follower's Action and the Tarjih
Abu Hanifa has two narrations: (1) make salam immediately, or (2) wait for the imam's salam. The author of al-Hidayah declares the second as the chosen (mukhtar) view.
The mukhtar view is to wait for the imam's salam to maintain some element of following.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ امام نے اگر پانچویں تکبیر کہی تو مقتدی اس پانچویں تکبیر میں امام کی پیروی نہ کرے کیونکہ چار سے زائد تکبیریں گذشتہ روایت کی وجہ سے منسوخ ہو چکی ہیں۔ امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر امام نے پانچویں تکبیر کہی تو مقتدی اس کی پیروی کرے گا۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چار تکبیرات سے زائد کا مسئلہ مختلف فیہ ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ حضرت علی نے نماز جنازہ میں چار کے بعد پانچویں تکبیر کہی تو مقتدیوں نے حضرت علی کی پیروی کی ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ صحابہ نے اس بارے میں مشورہ کیا اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی آخری نماز کی طرف رجوع کیا۔ پس حضرت علی کا پانچویں تکبیر کہنا منسوخ ہو گیا اور منسوخ کی پیروی کرنا غلط اور خطاء ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مقتدی جب پانچویں تکبیر میں امام کی متابعت نہیں کرے گا تو کیا کرے۔ اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے دور روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ مقتدی فور اسلام پھیر دے تا کہ پانچویں تکبیر میں امام کی مخالفت ثابت ہو۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ مقتدی امام کے سلام پھیرنے کا انتظار کرے۔ تا کہ سلام کے اندر متابعت ہو جائے۔ مصنف ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مختار یہی دوسری روایت ہے۔
Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: If the imam says a fifth takbir, the follower should not follow him in that fifth takbir because more than four takbirs are abrogated due to the previous narration. Imam Zufar said: If the imam says a fifth takbir, the follower will follow him. Imam Zufar's proof is that the issue of more than four takbirs is disputed; indeed it is narrated that Ali said a fifth takbir in funeral prayer and the followers followed him. Our response is that the Companions consulted about this matter and referred to the Prophet's final prayer. Thus Ali's saying the fifth takbir is abrogated, and following an abrogated practice is wrong and erroneous. As for what the follower should do when he does not follow the imam in the fifth takbir, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one is that the follower should immediately make salam to show opposition to the fifth takbir; the second is that he should wait for the imam's salam so that he follows him in the salam. The author of al-Hidayah says the chosen (mukhtar) is the second narration.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens if the imam, in funeral prayer, says a fifth takbir. The majority Hanafi position (al-Quduri) is that the follower should not follow because the fifth takbir is abrogated; the established practice from the Prophet's last funeral prayer is only four takbirs. Imam Zufar argues that since the issue is disputed among the Companions (citing the example of Ali), the follower may follow the imam. The Hanafi response is that the Companions ultimately resolved the issue by referring to the Prophet's final practice, thereby abrogating the fifth takbir. The text then mentions two narrations from Abu Hanifa about what the follower should do if he does not follow: (1) he should immediately make salam to break away, or (2) wait for the imam's salam to maintain some form of following. The author of al-Hidayah declares the second view as the relied-upon (mukhtar) position.

Key Terms
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred ruling among multiple opinions within the Hanafi school.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that was once valid but later superseded by a later ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Hidayah, what is the chosen (mukhtar) action for a follower when the imam says a fifth takbir in funeral prayer?
A) Follow the imam in the fifth takbir.
B) Immediately make salam.
C) Wait for the imam's salam.
D) Repeat the prayer alone.

Key Takeaway
The fifth takbir in funeral prayer is abrogated; the follower must not follow it, and the relied-upon Hanafi position is to wait for the imam's salam.

When a Latecomer Makes Up Missed Takbirs in Funeral Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on latecomer to funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a masbuq in funeral prayer and distinguish between the views of Abu Yusuf and the tarafain on when to make up missed takbirs.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, each takbir is like a rak'ah—missed takbirs are made up after the imam's salam.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement about funeral prayer procedure. While the dua for a minor child offers a related mercy, the real legal puzzle concerns timing: when a person joins late, should they immediately say the missed takbir or follow the imam and make it up later? The answer hinges on how we analogize takbirs to rak'ahs in regular prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: the masbuq (joins after imam has begun) and the mudrik (present but missed first takbir). Note the ruling for each.
The mudrik does not need to wait or make up the first takbir—he joins immediately.
2
Understand the tarafain’s ruling for masbuq
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the latecomer should follow the imam in remaining takbirs and then make up missed ones after the salam. Identify the analogy used: each takbir is like a rak'ah.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf’s opposing view and proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the latecomer should say the missed takbir immediately upon joining, analogizing to the opening takbir (takbir al-iftitah) in regular prayer.
He views the first takbir as unique, like the opening of the prayer.
4
Analyze the tarafain’s response
The tarafain rebut that the analogy of each takbir to a rak'ah is stronger, and the rule of making up before salam has been abrogated. This leads to making up after salam.
The difference is purely methodological: how to weigh analogies.
5
Apply the consensus on mudrik
If present from the start but missed the first takbir, he is a mudrik and should not wait; he simply joins the imam in the next takbir.
This is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب کتاب نے کہا ہے کہ دعائیں کرنا در حقیقت میت کے لئے مغفرت طلب کرنا ہے اور ثناء اور صلوٰۃ علی النبی سے ابتداء کرنا دعا کی سنت ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ نابالغ بچہ کے لئے استغفار نہ کرے کیونکہ مکلف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے گناہ کا صدور نہیں ہوا۔ البتہ یہ دعا پر سے اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً واجعله لنا ذخراً واجعله لنا شافعاً و مشفعاً
اگر کوئی شخص نماز جنازہ میں اس وقت شامل ہوا، جب امام ایک یا دو تکبیریں کہ چکا تو آنے والا شخص کوئی تکبیر نہ کہے بلکہ اس کے شامل ہونے کے بعد جب امام نے تکبیر کہی تو اس کے ساتھ یہ بھی تکبیر کہے اور فوت شدہ تکبیروں کی قضاء امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کرے یہ قول طرفین کا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ شامل ہوتے ہی فوت شدہ تکبیر کہہ لے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہلی تکبیر یعنی تکبیر افتتاح کے بعد آنے والا مسبوق کے مانند ہے۔ اور مسبوق تکبیر افتتاح شامل ہونے کے بعد ضرور کہتا ہے۔ لہذا یہ بھی کہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص بلاشبہ مسبوق کے مانند ہے لیکن نماز جنازہ کی ہر تکبیر بمنزلہ ایک رکعت کے ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے نماز جنازہ کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے اربع کا ربع الظہر ۔ اور یہ بات آپ کو معلوم ہے کہ مسبوق فوت شدہ رکعات کی قضا امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کرتا ہے نہ کہ پہلے کیونکہ سلام سے پہلے قضاء کرنے کا حکم منسوخ ہو چکا ہے۔
اور اگر ایک شخص ابتداء سے حاضر تھا مگر امام کے ساتھ تکبیر نہیں کہی تو یہ امام کی دوسری تکبیر کا بالاتفاق انتظار نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ مدرک کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔
The author of the book said: Prayers (dua) in reality are seeking forgiveness for the deceased, and beginning with praise and blessings on the Prophet is the sunnah of supplication. For this reason, one should not seek forgiveness (istighfar) for a minor child, because since he is not obligated, no sin has occurred from him. However, he should (instead) say this prayer: 'Allahummaj'alhu lana faratan waj'alhu lana dhukhra waj'alhu lana shafi'an wa mushaffa''.
If a person joins the funeral prayer when the imam has already said one or two takbirs, then the arriving person should not say any takbir (immediately), but after he joins, when the imam says a takbir, he should say that takbir with him, and he should make up the missed takbirs after the imam makes salam. This is the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf said: He should say the missed takbir immediately upon joining. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that after the first takbir (takbir al-iftitah), the arriving person is like a masbuq (latecomer), and a masbuq necessarily says the opening takbir after joining. Therefore he should also say it. The proof of the two is that this person is indeed like a masbuq, but each takbir in funeral prayer is like a rak'ah. For this reason, it is said about funeral prayer: 'Four (takbirs) are like four rak'ahs of Zuhr.' And you know that a masbuq makes up missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam, not before, because the ruling of making up before salam has been abrogated.
And if a person was present from the beginning but did not say the takbir with the imam, then he should not, by consensus, wait for the imam's second takbir. Because he is in the rank of a mudrik (one who catches the prayer).
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings for those who join late or miss the first takbir in funeral prayer. First, it begins with a note on dua: supplication in funeral prayer is for forgiveness, but for a minor child who is not sinful, one does not ask forgiveness (istighfar) but instead prays for the child to be a forerunner and treasure. Then it addresses the latecomer (masbuq): the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, referred to as 'tarafain') is that the latecomer should not immediately say the missed takbir upon joining, but should follow the imam in the remaining takbirs and then make up the missed ones after the imam's salam. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that since the first takbir is the opening takbir, the latecomer should say it immediately upon joining, analogizing to a regular prayer where the masbuq says the opening takbir upon joining. The response of the two is that each takbir in funeral prayer is analogous to a rak'ah, and in regular prayer, missed rak'ahs are made up after the imam's salam, not before. Therefore, the latecomer should follow the imam and then make up missed takbirs afterward. The passage then states a consensus ruling: if a person was present from the start but did not say the first takbir with the imam, he should not wait for the second takbir; he is considered a mudrik and should simply join the imam in the next takbir.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the prayer after the imam has already started, thus missing some parts.
مدرک (mudrik): A person who joins the prayer from the beginning but misses some actions through no fault? Here specifically one who was present from start but didn't say the first takbir with imam.
طرفین (tarafain): Refers to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) as opposed to Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the tarafain), how should a latecomer who joins after the imam has said one or two takbirs in funeral prayer act?
A) Recite the missed takbir immediately after joining
B) Join the imam in the next takbir and make up missed takbirs after the imam's salam
C) Wait for the imam's next takbir and then say all missed ones
D) Leave the prayer and start again

Key Takeaway
In funeral prayer, a latecomer should follow the imam in remaining takbirs and make up missed takbirs after salam, following the analogy of each takbir to a rak'ah.

Position of Imam Relative to Deceased in Funeral Prayer
Explains the Hanafi ruling on where the imam should stand relative to the deceased's body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the imam's standing position in funeral prayer and explain the preferred view with its proof and reconciliation.

Core Idea
The imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased — it symbolizes intercession for faith.

The placement of the imam during funeral prayer is a sunnah that carries symbolic meaning. In this lesson, we examine a dispute internal to the Hanafi school: while the relied-upon view is to stand opposite the chest for both men and women, a narration from Abu Hanifa suggests different positions for men and women. We will see how this conflict is resolved through careful interpretation of the evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the primary Hanafi position (chest for both) and the narrated position from Abu Hanifa (head for man, middle for woman).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not between madhhabs.
2
Analyze the proof for the chest position
The chest is the locus of the heart, which contains the light of faith. Standing there symbolizes intercession based on faith.
This is a rational (ma'nawi) proof linking position to meaning.
3
Examine the opposing proof
Anas ibn Malik reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood at the head for a man and the middle for a woman, and said it was sunnah.
This is a textual (naqli) proof that seems to contradict the first.
4
Apply the reconciliation
The commentary interprets Anas's action as circumstantial: the woman's funeral was not covered (nafsh-dar), so the Prophet stood between it and the people to shield it.
This interpretation preserves the chest position as the general sunnah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for practice is to stand opposite the chest for both males and females, as it is supported by stronger evidence and symbolic meaning.
The narration from Abu Hanifa is considered a specific case, not the general rule.
