ويقوم الذى يصلى على الرجل والمرأة بحذاء الصدر لانه موضع القلب وفيه نور الايمان فيكون القيام عنده اشارة الى الشفاعة لايمانه وعن ابى حنيفة ان يقوم من الرجل بحذاء راسه ومن المرأة بحذاء وسطها لان انسا فعل كذلك و قال هو السنة قلنا تاويله ان جنازتها لم تكن منعوشة فحال بينها وبينهم ترجمہ اور جو شخص مرد و عورت کی نماز جنازہ پڑھتا ہے وہ سینہ کے مقابل کھڑا ہو کیونکہ سینہ دل کی جگہ ہے اور دل میں نور ایمان ہے۔ پس اس کے پاس کھڑا ہونا اشارہ ہوگا کہ شفاعت اس کے ایمان کی وجہ سے ہے۔ ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ مرد کے جنازہ کے سر کے مقابل کھڑا ہو اور عورت کے وسط میں کھڑا ہو۔ کیونکہ حضرت انسؓ نے اسی طرح کیا ہے اور کہا کہ یہی سنت ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حضرت انس کے کلام کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ عورت کا جنازہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں نفش دار نہ ہوتا تھا تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم عورت کے جنازہ اور لوگوں کے درمیان حائل ہو جایا کرتے تھے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جنازہ مرد کا ہو یا عورت کا نماز کے وقت امام میت کے سینہ کے مقابل کھڑا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ سینہ قلب کا محل ہے اور قلب کے اندر نور ایمان ہوتا ہے۔ پس سینہ کے پاس کھڑا ہونا اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہوگا کہ شفاعت اس کے ایمان کی وجہ سے کی گئی ہے امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہ بھی مروی ہے کہ جنازہ اگر مرد کا ہو تو امام اس کے سر کے مقابل کھڑا ہو ۔ اور اگر عورت کا ہے تو اس کے وسط میں کھڑا ہو ۔ دلیل حدیث انس ہے روی عن نافع ابي غالب قال كنت في سكة المربد فمرت جنازة معها ناس كثير قالوا جنازة عبد الله بن عمير فتبعها فاذا انا برجل عليه كساء رقيق على رأسه خرقة تقيه من الشمس فقلت من
And the person who prays for the man and woman should stand opposite the chest, because it is the place of the heart, and in the heart is the light of faith. So standing near it indicates intercession for his faith. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he should stand for a man opposite his head, and for a woman opposite her middle, because Anas did so and said it is the sunnah. We say: The interpretation of (Anas's words) is that her funeral was not covered (with a canopy?), so he placed himself between it and them.
Translation: And the person who prays the funeral prayer for a man and a woman stands opposite the chest, because it is the place of the heart, and in the heart is the light of faith. So standing near it is an indication of intercession for his faith. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that for a man he stands opposite his head, and for a woman opposite her middle, because Anas did so and said it is the sunnah. We say: The interpretation of Anas's statement is that the woman's funeral was not covered (with a cloth?) in the time of the Prophet, so he used to come between the funeral and the people.
Explanation: The issue is that whether the funeral is of a male or female, at the time of prayer, the imam stands opposite the chest. The proof is that the chest is the place of the heart, and in the heart is the light of faith. So standing near the chest indicates that intercession is made due to his faith. It is also narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if the funeral is of a man, the imam stands opposite his head, and if it is of a woman, he stands opposite her middle. The proof is the hadith of Anas: It is narrated from Nafi' Abi Ghalib: I was in the lane of al-Mirbad when a funeral passed with many people. They said (it is) the funeral of Abdullah bin Umayr, so I followed it. Then I saw a man wearing a thin cloak, with a cloth on his head protecting from the sun. I said, 'Who...' (text ends).
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage discusses the position of the imam relative to the deceased during funeral prayer. The primary Hanafi view is that the imam should stand opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female, because the chest contains the heart, which is the seat of faith, and this positioning symbolizes intercession for the deceased's faith. However, a narration from Abu Hanifa states that for a man, the imam stands at the head, and for a woman, at the middle, based on the practice of Anas ibn Malik who reported it as sunnah. The commentary resolves this apparent contradiction by interpreting Anas's action: the reason he stood between the funeral and the people was that the woman's funeral was not covered (perhaps meaning no canopy or covering), so he shielded it. This interpretation reconciles the difference: the sunnah is to stand at the chest, and the narration from Abu Hanifa is clarified as a specific circumstance. The text then provides the beginning of a hadith from Nafi' Abi Ghalib to support the practice of standing at the chest, but the narration is cut off.

Key Terms
بحذاء الصدر (bihadha' al-sadr): Opposite the chest; the recommended position for the imam in funeral prayer.
نفش (nafsh): A covering or canopy? The text says the woman's funeral was not 'nafsh-dar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi mufta bihi position for the imam's standing in funeral prayer?
A) Opposite the head for a man and the middle for a woman
B) Opposite the chest for both
C) Opposite the feet for a man and the head for a woman
D) At the side of the bier

Key Takeaway
The imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased in funeral prayer, as it signifies intercession based on faith, and conflicting narrations are reconciled through contextual interpretation.

Du'a for a Minor Child in Janazah Prayer
Ruling statement with ta'lil on du'a for minor child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct du'a for a minor child in janazah prayer and explain why istighfar is not recited.

Core Idea
For a minor child in janazah, ask for blessing, not forgiveness—no sin, so no istighfar.

In janazah prayer, the du'a is central. The Hanafi school teaches that the essence of du'a for the deceased is seeking forgiveness. But for a child who has not reached puberty, there are no sins. So instead of istighfar, we recite a specific supplication asking Allah to make the child a forerunner and treasure for the parents. This lesson explains the reasoning and the correct wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
This passage addresses what du'a to recite for a minor child in janazah. The ruling is that one does not seek forgiveness but recites a specific supplication.
The act is part of the sunnah of janazah prayer.
2
Understand the ta'lil (reasoning)
The reason istighfar is omitted: a minor is not mukallaf, so no sin has been committed. Seeking forgiveness implies sin, which is inappropriate.
Mukallaf = accountable; reached puberty and sane.
3
Memorize the prescribed du'a
The du'a narrated from the Prophet ﷺ: 'Allahumma aj'alhu lana faratan wa aj'alhu lana dhukhran wa aj'alhu lana shafi'an wa mushaffa'an.'
This du'a asks for the child to be a predecessor, a treasure, and an intercessor.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school restricts istighfar for minors; other schools may allow general forgiveness du'as. Understand the grounds for ikhtilaf.
Ikhtilaf is legitimate; each school has its evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب کتاب نے کہا ہے کہ دعائیں کرنا در حقیقت میت کے لئے مغفرت طلب کرنا ہے اور ثناء اور صلوٰۃ علی النبی سے ابتداء کرنا دعا کی سنت ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ نابالغ بچہ کے لئے استغفار نہ کرے کیونکہ مکلف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے گناہ کا صدور نہیں ہوا۔ البتہ یہ دعا پر سے اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً واجعله لنا ذخراً واجعله لنا شافعاً و مشفعاً -
The author of the book said: Making supplications is in reality seeking forgiveness for the deceased, and beginning with praise and salawat upon the Prophet is the sunnah of supplication. For this reason, one should not seek forgiveness for a minor child, because due to not being mukallaf, sin has not emanated from him. However, instead of that, one should supplicate: 'O Allah, make him a predecessor for us, and make him a stored treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted for us.'
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the appropriate du'a for a minor child in janazah prayer. The author explains that the essence of du'a is seeking forgiveness (maghfirah) for the deceased. It is sunnah to begin the du'a with praise of Allah and salawat upon the Prophet. However, for a minor child who has not reached puberty (bulugh) and is not mukallaf (legally accountable), there are no sins to forgive. Therefore, instead of istighfar (asking forgiveness), one should make a specific du'a: 'O Allah, make him a forerunner (farat) for us, a stored treasure (dhukhur) for us, and an intercessor (shafi') whose intercession is accepted (mushaffa') for us.' This du'a is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that since the child has not committed sins, seeking forgiveness is inappropriate; rather, we ask for the child to be a source of benefit for the parents in the Hereafter.

Key Terms
مکلف (mukallaf): A person who has reached puberty and is legally accountable for their actions.
فرط (farat): A predecessor who goes ahead to prepare a place for others.
ذخر (dhukhur): A stored treasure or reserve of reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) اللهم اجعله لنا فرطاً وذخراً وشافعاً ومشفعاً
C) اللهم انا نسألك العفو والعافية
D) لا اله الا الله

Key Takeaway
For a minor child in janazah, ask Allah to make the child a forerunner and treasure for the parents, not seek forgiveness, as the child has no sins.

Imam's Position in Janazah Prayer: Chest, Head, or Waist?
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and hadith analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the primary Hanafi ruling on the imam's position in janazah prayer, identify the intra-Hanafi variant narration, and evaluate the evidence for each view.

Core Idea
The imam stands at the chest of the deceased — symbolizing intercession through faith.

This lesson examines a fiqh dispute within the Hanafi school: where exactly should the imam stand relative to the deceased during janazah prayer? The primary ruling places the imam opposite the chest, based on a wisdom-based reasoning linking the heart to faith. However, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa himself suggests a different position for men and women, supported by the practice of Anas ibn Malik. Understanding this ikhtilaf and its resolution is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
State the primary Hanafi position
Recall the core ruling: the imam stands opposite the chest (sadr) for both men and women. Understand the wisdom: the chest contains the heart, seat of faith, symbolizing intercession for the deceased's faith.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the variant narration from Abu Hanifa
Learn the alternate view: imam stands at the head for a man and at the waist (buttocks) for a woman. Note its attribution to a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa.
This is not the primary view but a valid ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the proof for the variant
Analyze the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: he stood at the head for a man and at the buttocks for a woman, and said this is the sunnah. The hadith is cited as the main evidence.
The hadith is ahad and zanni in thubut and dalala.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the interpretation offered by the author of al-Hidayah: Anas acted this way because the woman's funeral lacked a canopy, so he stood to screen her. However, the commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) rejects this because the hadith explicitly mentions a green canopy (n'ash akhdar).
The interpretation is considered weak, so the primary ruling stands.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: if the variant is followed, the imam changes position based on gender. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the chest for both, as determined by later Hanafi authorities.
Consistency and ease of practice favor the chest position.

The imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased. And the one who prays over a man and a woman stands opposite the chest because it is the place of the heart and in it is the light of faith, so standing near it is an indication of intercession for his faith. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he stands opposite the head of a man and opposite the middle of a woman because Anas did that and said it is the sunnah. We say: the interpretation is that her funeral was not in a canopy (na'sh), so he stood between her and the people. 
Translation: And the one who prays the janazah prayer of a man and a woman stands opposite the chest because the chest is the place of the heart and in the heart is the light of faith. So standing near it is an indication that intercession is due to his faith. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he stands opposite the head of a man and opposite the middle of a woman. Because Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) did that and said that is the sunnah. We say: the interpretation of Anas's statement is that the woman's funeral at the time of the Prophet ﷺ was not covered with a canopy, so the Prophet ﷺ used to stand between the woman's funeral and the people. 
Explanation: The issue is that whether the deceased is a man or a woman, at the time of prayer the imam should stand opposite the chest of the deceased. The proof is that the chest is the place of the heart and in the heart is the light of faith. So standing near the chest is an indication that intercession is due to his faith. It is also narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if the deceased is a man, the imam stands opposite his head, and if it is a woman, he stands opposite her middle. The proof is the hadith of Anas: Nafi' Abu Ghalib narrated: I was in the alley of al-Mirbad when a funeral procession passed with many people. They said it was the funeral of Abdullah ibn Umayr, so I followed. I saw a man wearing a thin cloak with a cloth on his head to protect from the sun. I asked who that villager was; they said Anas ibn Malik. When the funeral was placed on the ground, Anas stood to pray, and I was behind him with nothing between us. He stood at the head and said four takbirs, neither prolonging nor hastening. Then he was about to sit when they said, 'O Abu Hamza, there is also an Ansari woman's funeral.' They brought it forward, and it had a green canopy (na'sh). He stood near her buttocks (i.e., middle) and prayed over her similarly to his prayer over the man. Then he sat. Al-'Ala' ibn Ziyad asked, 'O Abu Hamza, did the Messenger of Allah ﷺ pray over the funerals like your prayer, saying four takbirs, standing at the head of a man and at the buttocks of a woman?' He said, 'Yes.' That is, narrated from Nafi', he said that a funeral passed by an alley with many people. They said it was the funeral of Abdullah ibn Umayr. I followed and saw a man with a thin cloak and a cloth on his head. I asked who that villager was; they said Anas ibn Malik. When the funeral was placed, Anas stood to pray, and I was behind him with nothing between us. He stood at the head and said four takbirs, neither long nor quick. Then he began to sit, and they said, 'O Abu Hamza, there is an Ansari woman's funeral.' They brought it close, and it had a green canopy. He stood at her buttocks (i.e., middle) and prayed as he prayed over the man. Then he sat. Al-'Ala' asked if the Prophet did that, and Anas said yes. The author of Hidayah says that Anas declared this method as sunnah. The author of Hidayah, interpreting the hadith, said the Ansari woman's funeral did not have a canopy, meaning a coffin-like structure, which would have screened the woman's aura, so he stood in the middle to screen between the woman and the people. But this interpretation is not reliable because the hadith explicitly mentions 'and upon it a green canopy'.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on where the imam should stand during janazah prayer, along with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The primary Hanafi position is that the imam stands opposite the chest (sadr) of the deceased, whether man or woman. The reason (wisdom) is that the chest contains the heart, which is the seat of faith (iman), and standing there symbolizes that intercession (shafa'ah) is being sought for the deceased's faith. However, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa states that the imam should stand opposite the head of a man and opposite the middle (waist/buttocks) of a woman. This is supported by the practice of Anas ibn Malik (ra), who prayed at the head of a man and at the buttocks of a woman. The author (of Hidayah) responds that Anas's action is to be interpreted as an exception for a specific reason: the woman's funeral did not have a canopy (na'sh) covering the body, so Anas stood at the middle to screen her from the view of the people, as the Prophet ﷺ used to do. However, the commentator (of Ashraf al-Hidayah) rejects this interpretation because the hadith explicitly states that the woman's funeral had a green canopy (n'ash akhdar), which would have provided cover, thus the need for screening is not present. Therefore, the primary ruling remains that the imam stands at the chest for both, and the narration from Abu Hanifa is either a rare transmission or interpreted in light of specific circumstances.

Key Terms
بحذاء الصدر (bihidha' al-sadr): Opposite the chest; the position where the imam stands during janazah prayer.
شفاعت (shafa'ah): Intercession; here it refers to the Prophet's intercession for the deceased based on their faith.
نعش (na'sh): A canopy or bier over the deceased, especially for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi position regarding where the imam stands during janazah prayer?
A) At the head for men, at the waist for women
B) Opposite the chest for both men and women
C) At the feet of the deceased
D) Any position is permissible

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased during janazah prayer for both men and women.

Imam's Position in Funeral Prayer: Sunnah from the Hadith of Anas
Hadith of Anas ibn Malik with commentary and refutation of a ta'wil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's standing position for male and female funerals and explain why the explicit hadith overrides the ta'wil of Sahib al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
For male corpse: imam at head; for female: imam at hips – established by prophetic practice.

This lesson examines a crucial hadith narrated by Anas ibn Malik that directly prescribes the imam's standing position in funeral prayer. The hadith is clear, but a later ta'wil by the author of Al-Hidayah attempted to qualify it. By studying the hadith and the refutation, you will understand how explicit textual evidence (nass) prevails over speculative interpretation in Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the hadith
Read the hadith carefully. Note where Anas stood for the male corpse (at the head) and for the female corpse (at the hips/middle). This is the action that Anas confirmed was the practice of the Prophet (PBUH).
The hadith uses 'ind 'ajizatiha' meaning at her hips.
2
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The hadith is a sunnah ahad (single narration) but acts as a clear proof (dalil) for the ruling. The chain is sound: from Anas via Nafi'. The witness of Al-‘Ala’ ibn Ziyad confirms that Anas attributed this to the Prophet.
The proof is explicit action (fi'l) and verbal confirmation (taqrir).
3
Understand the ta'wil of Sahib al-Hidayah
Sahib al-Hidayah interpreted that the woman had no canopy (na‘sh), so the middle position was due to a barrier. This interpretation aimed to preserve modesty, but it contradicts the text.
The ta'wil was based on an assumption not in the hadith.
4
Analyse the refutation
The commentator refutes the ta'wil by pointing to the explicit words 'upon her a green canopy' (wa 'alayha na‘sh akhdar). Thus the woman was covered, so the barrier argument collapses. The explicit text takes precedence.
This demonstrates the principle: 'al-‘ibrah bi 'umum al-lafz la bi khusus al-sabab' (consideration is given to the general wording, not to the specific occasion).
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling is that the imam stands at the head for a male corpse and at the middle (hips) for a female corpse, as per the explicit Sunnah. This is the position of the majority and is acted upon.
This ruling is considered sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah).

Source Text

هذا الدهقان قالوا انس بن مالك قال فلما وضعت الجنازة قام انس فصلى عليها و انا خلفه لا يحول بيني و بینه شيء فقام عند رأسه و كبر اربع تكبيرات لم يطل و لم يسرع ثم ذهب يقعد فقالوا يا ابا حمزة المرأة الانصارية فقربوها و عليها نعش اخضر فقام عند عجيزتها فصلى عليها نحو صلوتة على الرجل ثم جلس فقال العلاء بن زياد يا ابا حمزة هكذا كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلى على الجنائز كصلوتك يكبر عليها اربعاً ويقوم عند رأس الرجل و عجيزة المرأة قال نعم یعنی نافع سے مروی ہے کہ نافع نے کہا کہ گلی سے ایک جنازہ جس کے ساتھ بہت سے لوگ تھے ، گذرا۔ لوگوں نے کہا کہ یہ عبداللہ بن عمیر کا جنازہ ہے ( نافع کہتے ہیں کہ ) میں بھی جنازہ کے ساتھ چل دیا میں نے دیکھا کہ ایک آدمی جس کے بدن پر بار یک چادر اور دھوپ سے بچاؤ کے لئے سر پر ایک کپڑا رکھا ہوا ہے۔ میں نے کہا کہ یہ کون دہقانی اور گاوندی ہے۔ لوگوں نے کہا کہ یہ انس بن مالک ہیں۔ نافع کہتے ہیں کہ جب جنازہ زمین پر رکھ دیا گیا تو انس نے کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھائی اور میں آپ کے پیچھے تھا کہ میرے اور آپ کے درمیان کوئی چیز حائل نہ تھی (پس میں نے دیکھا کہ ) آپ جنازہ کے سر کے پاس کھڑے ہوئے اور چار تکبیریں کہیں اس طور پر کہ نہ طویل تھیں اور نہ جلدی کی ، پھر آپ بیٹھنے لگے تو لوگوں نے کہا اے ابوحمزہ ( انس بن مالک) ایک انصاری عورت کا جنازہ بھی ہے۔ پس لوگوں نے اس کو انس کے قریب کیا اور اس پر ایک سبز رنگ کی نعش ( مردہ کی چار پائی جس پر صندوق سا بنا رہتا ہے ) تھی آپ اس کے چوتڑوں کے پاس یعنی وسط میں کھڑے ہوئے اور نماز پڑھائی جیسے مرد کی پڑھائی تھی پھر آپ بیٹھ گئے پس علاء بن زیاد نے کہا کہ اے ابو حمزہ کیا رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم بھی جنازوں پر اسی طرح نماز پڑھتے تھے تو انس نے کہا کہ ہاں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ حضرت انس نے اس طریقہ کو مسنون قرار دیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس حدیث کی تاویل کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ انصاری عورت کے جنازہ پر نعش نہیں تھی یعنی وہ صندوق نما تابوت نہیں تھا۔ جس سے عورت کا ستر ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس عورت اور لوگوں کے درمیان حائل ہونے کی وجہ سے وسط میں کھڑے ہو گئے۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ کی یہ تاویل اس لئے معتبر نہیں ہے کہ حدیث میں بصراحت و عليها نعش اخضر کا لفظ موجود ہے۔
This is the village elder. They said: Anas ibn Malik. He said: When the funeral was placed, Anas stood and prayed over it while I was behind him with nothing between us. He stood at its head and said four takbirs, not prolonging nor hastening. Then he went to sit. They said: O Abu Hamza, the Ansari woman. So they brought her forward, and she had a green canopy. He stood at her hips and prayed over her like his prayer over the man. Then he sat. Al-‘Ala’ ibn Ziyad said: O Abu Hamza, did the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) pray over funerals like your prayer, saying four takbirs, standing at the man’s head and the woman’s hips? He said: Yes. Meaning: It is narrated from Nafi‘ that Nafi‘ said: A funeral with many people passed from an alley. They said: This is the funeral of ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Umayr. I went along with the funeral. I saw a man with a single cloth on his body and a cloth on his head for sun protection. I said: Who is this villager? They said: This is Anas ibn Malik. Nafi‘ said: When the funeral was placed on the ground, Anas stood and led the prayer, and I was behind him with nothing between us. So I saw him stand at the head of the funeral and say four takbirs such that he did not prolong nor hasten. Then he began to sit. They said: O Abu Hamza, there is also the funeral of an Ansari woman. So they brought her close to him, and she had a green canopy (a bier with a box-like structure). He stood at her hips, i.e., middle, and prayed over her like his prayer over the man. Then he sat. Al-‘Ala’ ibn Ziyad said: O Abu Hamza, did the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) pray over funerals in this manner? Anas said: Yes. The author of Hidayah says that Anas declared this method to be Sunnah. The author of Hidayah, interpreting this hadith, said: The Ansari woman’s funeral did not have a nakhsh (canopy/box), i.e., a box-like coffin that conceals the woman’s awrah. Therefore, due to the barrier between the woman and the people, he stood in the middle. But the author of Hidayah’s interpretation is not acceptable because the hadith explicitly mentions the words 'upon her a green canopy'.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration establishing the Sunnah position of the imam in funeral prayer. The hadith is transmitted by Nafi‘ from Anas ibn Malik. It shows that for a male corpse, the imam stands at the head; for a female corpse, at the hips (middle). The author of Hidayah attempted a ta’wil, suggesting the woman in the hadith had no canopy, hence barrier necessitated middle position. However, the commentator refutes this, noting the explicit mention of a green canopy. Thus the relied-upon Hanafi ruling: the imam stands at the head for men and at the middle for women, as per the clear Sunnah.

Key Terms
عجيزة (‘ajizah): The hips or middle part of the female body; the place where the imam stands for a female corpse.
نعش (na‘sh): A bier with a canopy or box-like structure covering the corpse.

Key Takeaway

Funeral Prayer While Mounted: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Ruling with qiyas and istihsan analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates funeral prayer on a mount, using the distinction between qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer resembles both du'a and salat; the tahrimah makes it like salat, requiring standing.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi case where two legal reasoning methods yield opposite results: qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). Understanding why istihsan overrides qiyas in this ruling strengthens your grasp of Hanafi usul and the weight of precaution (ihtiyat) in ibadat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal methods
Recognize that the passage presents two competing analogies: qiyas (funeral prayer is du'a) and istihsan (it is like salat).
Both are valid methods; the conflict is resolved by tarjih.
2
Trace the qiyas argument
See how qiyas aligns funeral prayer with du'a because it lacks ruku' and sujud, concluding mounted prayer is valid.
This is the apparent analogy (qiyas jali).
3
Trace the istihsan argument
Note that istihsan considers the presence of tahrimah (opening takbir) and the requirement of conditions like qiyam, making it like salat.
Istihsan relies on the hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) and precaution.
4
Identify the tarjih (preference)
The text explicitly prefers istihsan over qiyas; the mufta bihi is that funeral prayer while mounted is invalid without an excuse.
This is a standard Hanafi method: istihsan overrides qiyas when a stronger proof (here, the resemblance to salat) exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سواری پر نماز جنازہ پڑھنے کا حکم فان صلوا على جنازة ركبانا اجزاهم فى القياس لانها دعاء وفى الاستحسان لاتجزيهم لانها صلواة من وجه لوجود التحريمة فلا يجوز تركه من غير عذر احتياطا ترجمہ اگر لوگوں نے جنازہ پر سواری کی حالت میں نماز پڑھی تو قیاس کے مطابق ان کی نماز جائز ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ یہ دعا ہے اور استحسانا جائز نہیں ہوئی کیونکہ یہ حریمہ کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے من وجہ نماز ہے لہذا احتیاطاً بغیر عذر کے اس کا ترک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح سواری پر سوار ہو کر نماز جنازہ پڑھنا قیا سا تو جائز ہے لیکن استحسانا جائز نہیں ہے قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ در حقیقت دعا کا نام ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ میں نہ قرآت ہے نہ رکوع اور سجدہ پس جس طرح دوسری دعاؤں کا پڑھنا سواری پر جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح نماز جنازہ بھی جائز ہے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ من وجہ نماز ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز جنازہ کے لئے تحریمہ پایا جاتا ہے اور وقت کے علاوہ تمام وہ شرطیں ضروری ہیں جو دوسری نمازوں کے لئے ضروری ہیں۔ پس بلا عذر احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ قیام کو ترک نہ کیا جائے اور سواری پر نماز پڑھنے کی صورت میں چونکہ قیام ترک کرنا پڑتا ہے اس لئے سواری پر نماز جنازہ پڑھنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
Ruling on praying funeral prayer while mounted: If they pray over a funeral while mounted, it suffices them according to qiyas because it is a supplication; but according to istihsan it does not suffice them because it is prayer in one respect due to the presence of the tahrimah, so leaving it without excuse is not permissible as a precaution. Translation: If people pray funeral prayer while mounted, then according to qiyas their prayer is valid because it is a supplication; and according to istihsan it is not valid because it is prayer in one respect due to the presence of tahrimah, therefore as a precaution it is not permissible to leave it without excuse. Explanation: Performing funeral prayer while mounted is permissible according to qiyas but not according to istihsan. The reason for qiyas is that funeral prayer is in reality a supplication; this is why there is no recitation, bowing, or prostration in it. Just as other supplications are permissible while mounted, so too is funeral prayer. The reason for istihsan is that funeral prayer is prayer in one respect because the tahrimah is present in it, and besides time, all conditions necessary for other prayers are necessary. Thus without excuse, precaution is not to leave standing; and when praying while mounted, since standing must be omitted, it is not permissible to pray funeral prayer while mounted.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on performing funeral prayer while riding an animal. The text first gives the Arabic ruling from al-Hidayah, followed by translation and commentary. The ruling employs two legal reasoning methods: qiyas and istihsan. According to qiyas (analogy), funeral prayer is analogous to du'a (supplication) because it lacks ruku' and sujud, so riding is permitted. According to istihsan (juristic preference), funeral prayer is considered prayer (salat) in one respect because it begins with tahrimah and requires conditions like qiblah, purity, etc. Therefore, standing is obligatory, and riding without excuse invalidates it. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of istihsan: it is not valid without a valid excuse (e.g., illness, fear). This shows the Hanafi method of preferring istihsan over qiyas when textual and rational considerations weigh against the analogy.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits worldly actions and initiates the prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: preferring a hidden analogy or exceptional ruling over an obvious qiyas due to a stronger textual or rational proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, is it valid to perform funeral prayer while riding an animal without an excuse?
A) Yes, it is valid because it is du'a
B) No, it is invalid because standing is required
C) Yes, but only if the mount is still
D) No, but it can be repeated later

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school invalidates funeral prayer while mounted without an excuse, overriding the qiyas of du'a with the istihsan of salat-like requirements.

Permission and Announcement in Funeral Prayer
Definition of rulings on permission and announcement in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking permission (idhn) and announcing (adhan) for funeral prayer, and identify when announcement is recommended.

Core Idea
Permission and announcement in funeral prayer are permissible; announcement is mustahsan for pious individuals.

This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses two variant readings concerning funeral prayer. The first deals with permission from the wali, the second with making an announcement. Understanding these variants helps clarify the Hanafi position on these practices, which have implications for funeral arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two variant texts
The passage presents two versions: 'la ba'sa bil-adhani' and 'la ba'sa bil-idhni'. Recognize that each has different implications.
2
Explain the ruling on permission (idhn)
The wali has the right to lead the funeral prayer or delegate it. He may also permit attendees to leave after prayer. The ruling is permissibility.
3
Explain the ruling on announcement (adhan)
Announcement of the funeral is also permissible. Some later Hanafi scholars considered it recommended (mustahsan) for righteous individuals whose funeral attracts many.
This is based on a hadith and the practice of the Salaf.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools like the Maliki may disapprove of announcing funerals due to association with pre-Islamic customs. The Hanafi school distinguishes by context.

نماز جنازہ کے لئے ولی سے اجازت لینے کا حکم ولا باس بالاذان فى صلوة الجنازة لان التقدم حق الولى فيملك ابطاله بتقديم غيره وفي بعض النسخ لاباس بالاذن اى الاعلام وهو ان يعلم بعضهم بعضا ليقضوا حقه ترجمہ اور نماز جنازہ میں اجازت کا مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ امام کا ہونا ولی کا حق ہے پس وہ دوسرے کو آگے بڑھا کر اپنے حق کو باطل کر سکتا ہے اور بعض نسخوں میں ہے کہ نماز جنازہ میں اذان یعنی اعلان کا کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے ۔ اور اعلام یہ ہے کہ بعض لوگ دوسرے کو آگاہ کر دیں تا کہ وہ میت کا حق ادا کریں۔ تشریح متن کے دو نسخے ہیں۔ ایک تو لا باس بالاذن في صلوة الجنازة دوم لا بأس بالاذان ۔ پہلے نسخہ کی بنیاد پر عبارت کے دو مطلب ہوں گے۔ ایک یہ کہ ولی اگر کسی دوسرے کو نماز جنازہ پڑھانے کی اجازت دے دے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ امامت کا حق ولی کو ہے۔ پس ولی میت اگر دوسرے کو امام بنا کر اپنا حق مٹانا چاہے تو مٹا سکتا ہے۔ دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ سے فراغت کے بعد ولی اگر لوگوں کو گھر واپس جانے کی اجازت دے دے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ تدفین سے پہلے بغیر ولی کی اجازت کے لوگوں کا گھر واپس جانا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرے نسخہ کی بنیاد پر عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہوگا کہ نماز جنازہ کی اطلاع دینے اور لوگوں کو باخبر کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ قال اذا مات احدكم فاذ نونى بالصلوۃ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب تم میں سے کوئی مرجائے تو مجھے کو نماز کی اطلاع دینا۔ بعض متأخرین نے اس شخص کی نماز جنازہ کے لئے بازاروں میں اعلان کرنے کو ستحسن قرار دیا ہے جس کی نماز کے لئے لوگ راغب ہوں جیسے زاہد اور علما ء۔
Ruling on seeking permission from the wali for funeral prayer: There is no harm in permission [idhn] in funeral prayer because leadership is the right of the wali, so he can nullify it by presenting another. In some copies: there is no harm in the call [adhan], i.e., announcement, which is that some inform others so that they may fulfill the deceased's right. Translation: And there is no harm in permission in funeral prayer. Because being imam is the right of the wali, so he can nullify his right by sending another forward. And in some copies: there is no harm in the call (adhan), i.e., announcement, which is that some inform others so that they may fulfill the deceased's right. Explanation: There are two versions of the text. One: 'La ba'sa bil-idhni fi salatil-janazah'; second: 'La ba'sa bil-adhani'. According to the first version, there are two meanings: (1) If the wali permits another to lead the funeral prayer, there is no harm, because the right of imamat belongs to the wali; he can nullify his right by making another imam. (2) After the funeral prayer, if the wali permits people to return home, there is no harm, because before burial it is not correct for people to return without the wali's permission. According to the second version, the meaning is that there is no harm in announcing (informing) the funeral prayer. The hadith: 'When one of you dies, inform me of the prayer.' Some later scholars considered it good to announce in the marketplaces for the funeral prayer of a person whom people would be keen to pray for, such as ascetics and scholars.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage clarifies the permissibility of permission (idhn) and announcement (adhan) regarding funeral prayer. The text discusses variant readings of al-Hidayah. The first variant concerns the wali's permission: the wali (guardian) has the right to lead the funeral prayer or delegate it to another. He can also permit attendees to leave after prayer. The second variant concerns making an announcement (adhan) to call people to the funeral prayer. This is considered recommended (mustahsan) for pious individuals whose funeral would attract many participants. The hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) is cited as a basis for informing others. Thus, the ruling is that both permission and announcement are permissible and, in some cases, recommended.

Key Terms
اذن (idhn): Permission from the wali to another to lead the funeral prayer or to allow people to leave.
اذان (adhan): Announcement or call to inform people about the funeral prayer, especially for virtuous persons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what is the ruling on the wali permitting another person to lead the funeral prayer?
A) It is not allowed because imamat is the wali's exclusive right
B) It is permissible; the wali can delegate his right
C) It is recommended but not obligatory
D) It is invalid without prior consent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, both seeking permission from the wali and announcing the funeral prayer are permissible, with announcement being recommended for righteous individuals.

Ruling on Funeral Prayer in a Mosque
Ruling with hadith and intra-madhhab dispute on mosque funeral

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer in a mosque, cite the hadith proof, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute and the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer inside a mosque is makruh in the Hanafi school: the hadith of no reward guides this.

Should funeral prayer be performed inside the mosque? The Hanafi school answers with caution: the prayer is valid but disliked. This lesson unpacks the evidence—the Prophet's hadith and the mosque's intended purpose—and examines a dispute among later Hanafi scholars about scenarios where the deceased is outside the mosque. We also compare the position of Imam al-Shafi'i, who sees no dislike at all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its primary evidence
The matn states: 'Do not pray over a deceased in a mosque in congregation' and immediately cites a hadith. Identify that the ruling is makruh (disliked) and that the hadith is the core proof.
The hadith: 'Whoever prays over a funeral in a mosque has no reward for him.'
2
Analyze the secondary reasons
The author gives two additional reasons: mosques are built for obligatory prayers, and there is a risk of soiling the mosque with najasah. Understand how these reinforce the ruling.
These reasons are ancillary, not independent proofs.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi scholarly difference
The text reports that when the deceased is outside the mosque, the mashayikh (Hanafi scholars) differed: some said makruh, others said not makruh. This is an internal ikhtilaf.
The commentary from al-‘Inayah clarifies two sub-scenarios.
4
Examine the Shafi‘i position
Imam Shafi‘i holds that funeral prayer is not makruh in any case—neither when the deceased is inside nor outside. The text cuts off, but the issue is clear.
The Shafi‘i position is based on other evidence (e.g., ‘A’ishah’s practice).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis consider the prayer makruh and reward diminished; Shafi‘is consider it fully permissible with full reward. The practical consequence is a difference in recommended practice.
Both schools agree the prayer is valid if performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Ruling on performing funeral prayer in a mosque: Do not pray over a deceased in a mosque in congregation because of the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever prays over a funeral in a mosque, there is no reward for him.' And because the mosque was built for performing obligatory prayers. And because there is a likelihood of soiling the mosque. And when the deceased is outside the mosque, the mashayikh have disagreed. Translation: And no funeral prayer should be performed on a deceased in a mosque in congregation because the Prophet said: Whoever prays over a funeral in a mosque has no reward. And because the mosque was built for performing obligatory prayers. And because there is likelihood of soiling the mosque. And in the case when the deceased is outside the mosque, the mashayikh have differed. Explanation: The author of 'Inayah solved this text stating: If only the funeral is in the mosque while the imam and some people are outside, and the rest are inside, then by consensus it is not makruh. If only the funeral is outside and the imam and all people are inside, the mashayikh have differed: some opine karahah, some no karahah. Imam Shafi'i said: It is not makruh in any case, i.e., only the funeral...
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage discusses the prohibition of performing funeral prayer inside a mosque. The Arabic matn states the ruling: it is not to be done in congregation. The proof is a hadith: 'Whoever prays over a funeral in the mosque, there is no reward for him.' Additional reasons: the mosque is for obligatory prayers, and there is risk of najasah soiling it. The text then addresses a scenario when the deceased is outside the mosque. The commentary from 'Inayah clarifies: if the corpse is inside and the imam outside, it is not makruh by consensus. If the corpse is outside and the imam and all followers inside, the mashayikh (Hanafi scholars) differ. Some say makruh, some not. Imam Shafi'i holds it not makruh in any situation. The text cuts off before completing the Shafi'i statement. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is makruh to pray inside the mosque when the deceased is also inside; when the deceased is outside, there is ikhtilaf but the more precautionary view is karahah.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Legal disapproval; in this context, makruh tanzih (avoiding is better but not sinful).
مسجد (masjid): Mosque: a place built for performing the five daily prayers and other acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible without any dislike
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Funeral prayer inside a mosque is makruh tanzih according to the Hanafi school; the hadith 'no reward' and the mosque's primary purpose support this ruling.

Permission and Announcement in Funeral Prayer
Clarification of two manuscript readings on permission and announcement in funeral prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on the guardian's permission (idhn) for leading the funeral prayer and the permissibility of announcement (adhan) for the funeral, and DISTINGUISH between the two manuscript versions.

Core Idea
The guardian may delegate the funeral prayer or allow attendees to leave, and announcing a death is permissible.

This passage from the classical Hanafi text presents two manuscript readings of a short phrase concerning the funeral prayer. One version discusses the guardian's permission (idhn) to delegate imamah or to allow departure after the prayer. The other version addresses the announcement (adhan) to gather people for the funeral. Understanding these rulings is important for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh in funeral arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manuscript versions
The text notes two readings: 'la ba'sa bi al-idhn' (permission) and 'la ba'sa bi al-adhan' (call/announcement). Recognize that the Arabic differs by one letter.
2
Interpret the first version (idhn)
The commentator gives two interpretations: (a) the guardian may permit another to lead the funeral prayer; (b) after the prayer, the guardian may permit attendees to leave before burial.
3
Interpret the second version (adhan)
This refers to announcing the death to inform people so they can attend the funeral prayer.
4
Connect to the hadith and later practice
The Prophet requested to be informed of a death. Later Hanafi scholars considered it commendable (istihsan) to announce in the market for pious persons.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ اور نماز جنازہ میں اجازت کا مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ امام کا ہونا ولی کا حق ہے پس وہ دوسرے کو آگے بڑھا کر اپنے حق کو باطل کر سکتا ہے اور بعض نسخوں میں ہے کہ نماز جنازہ میں اذان یعنی اعلان کا کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے ۔ اور اعلام یہ ہے کہ بعض لوگ دوسرے کو آگاہ کر دیں تا کہ وہ میت کا حق ادا کریں۔

There is no harm in the call (adhan) for the funeral prayer, because leadership is the right of the guardian, so he can nullify it by putting forward another. And in some copies: there is no harm in permission (al-idhn), i.e., informing, and that is that some inform others so that they may fulfill the right of the deceased. Translation: And there is no harm in permission in the funeral prayer. Because the imam's position is the right of the guardian, so he can nullify his right by putting forward another. And in some copies: there is no harm in the call (adhan) in the funeral prayer, i.e., announcement. And informing is that some people inform others so that they may fulfill the right of the deceased. Explanation: The text has two versions. One is 'la ba'sa bi al-idhn fi salat al-janazah' and the second is 'la ba'sa bi al-adhan'. Based on the first version, the phrase has two meanings. One is that if the guardian gives permission to another to lead the funeral prayer, there is no harm. Because the right of imamah belongs to the guardian. So the guardian of the deceased, if he wants to cancel his right by making someone else imam, he can cancel it. The second meaning is that after completion of the funeral prayer, if the guardian gives permission to the people to return home, there is no harm. Because before burial, without the guardian's permission, people returning home is not correct. And based on the second version, the phrase means that there is no harm in giving information about the funeral prayer and making people aware. He said: 'When one of you dies, inform me of the prayer.' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you dies, inform me of the prayer.' Some latter scholars have considered it commendable to announce in the markets for the funeral prayer of a person for whom people are desirous, such as a pious person or a scholar.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn, expanded by the commentator. The author presents two manuscript versions of the same phrase: one with 'idhn' (permission) and one with 'adhan' (call to prayer/announcement). Under the first version, two interpretations are given: (1) the guardian of the deceased may give permission to someone else to lead the funeral prayer, as the right of imamah belongs to him, and he may relinquish it; (2) after the funeral prayer, the guardian may give permission to the attendees to leave, as it is not proper to leave before burial without the guardian's consent. Under the second version, the meaning is that it is permissible to announce the death and inform people to come for the funeral prayer. The commentator cites a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) requested to be informed of a death. Later scholars (mutakkhirin) considered it commendable (istihsan) to announce in the marketplace for the funeral of a pious scholar. The key lesson is that the guardian's right over the funeral arrangements is recognized, and announcements are allowed to gather participants.

Key Terms
اذن (idhn): Permission granted by the guardian to another to lead the funeral prayer or to leave after burial
اذان (adhan): Call or announcement to inform people about the death and funeral prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) It is only allowed if the deceased was a scholar.

Key Takeaway
The guardian has the right to delegate the funeral prayer leadership and may permit attendees to leave; additionally, announcing a death is permissible to gather participants.

Funeral Prayer in the Mosque: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents Hanafi ruling against funeral prayer in mosque with proof and rebuttal of Shafi'i evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer in the mosque, identify the Shafi'i counter-evidence, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal using dalil and contextual analysis.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer inside a mosque is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school, even though Shafi'is permit it.

Funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a collective obligation, but where should it be performed? This lesson examines a well-known ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi position, as stated in al-Hidayah, is that it is disliked (makruh tahrimi) to bring the deceased into the mosque for the prayer, supported by a hadith of Abu Hurayrah and the principle that mosques are built for the five daily prayers. The Shafi'i school, relying on actions of the Prophet and 'A'ishah, considers it permissible. We will analyze the proofs and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
From the matn: funeral prayer in congregation is not performed for a deceased in a mosque. This is the ruling. Note the exception: if the janazah is outside the mosque and people are inside, there is no dislike according to some scholars.
The text says 'makruh' generally; the Hanafi school clarifies it as makruh tahrimi.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is permissible in all cases, even with the janazah inside. He cites 'A'ishah ordering Sa'd's janazah into the mosque and the Prophet's prayer over Suhayl ibn al-Bayda' in the mosque.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof consists of three points: (1) Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is no reward for him.' (2) Mosques are built for the five obligatory prayers, not funerals. (3) Potential impurity (taluwih) from the janazah.
The hadith is a dalil naqli of ahad nature but sufficient for prohibition.
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i evidence
First, 'A'ishah's action was criticized by the Companions, showing the known dislike. Second, the Prophet's prayer was during i'tikaf (excuse) and the janazah was actually placed outside, so he prayed from inside while it was outside. Thus neither incident contradicts the hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi masajid, the janazah is placed outside the prayer hall or in a designated area outside. Shafi'i masajid may allow it inside. This affects the fiqh of the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يصلى على ميت في مسجد جماعة لقول النبي من صلى على جنازة في المسجد فلا اجر له ولانه بنى لاداء المكتوبات ولانه يحتمل تلويث المسجد وفيما اذا كان الميت خارج المسجد اختلف المشائخ ترجمہ اور کسی میت پر مسجد جماعت میں نماز نہ پڑھی جائے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے مسجد میں جنازہ پر نماز پڑھی اس کے واسطے ثواب نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ مسجد تو ادائے فرائض کے لئے بنائی گئی ہے اور اس لئے کہ اس میں مسجد کے آلودہ ہونے کا احتمالہ ہے اور اس صورت میں جبکہ میت مسجد سے باہر ہو تو مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب عنایہ نے اس عبارت کو حل کریت ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر فقط جنازہ مسجد میں ہو اور امام اور کچھ لوگ مسجد سے باہر ہوا۔ اور باقی مسجد میں ہوں تو بالا تفاق مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اور گر فقط جنازہ مسجد سے باہر ہو اور امام اور تمام لوگ مسجد میں ہوں تو مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے۔ بعض کراہت کے قائل ہیں اور بعض عدم کراہت کے ۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ کسی حال میں مکروہ نہیں ہے یعنی فقط جنازہ ا مسجد میں ہو تب بھی اس پر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب سعد بن ابی وقاص کی وفات ہوئی تو صدیقہ عائشہ نے حکم کیا کہ ان کے جنازہ کو مسجد میں داخل کیا جائے حتی کہ اس پر تمام ازواج مطہرات نے نماز پڑھی۔ پھر حضرت عائشہ نے اپنے اردگرد کے بعض لوگوں سے کہا کہ کیا لوگوں ہمارے اس فعل پر عیب لگایا ہے۔ انہوں نے کہا کہ ہاں ( لوگوں کو اس پر اعتراض ہے ) حضرت عائشہ نے کہا کہ لوگ کس قدر جلد فراموش کر گئے کہ رسول اللہ ا نے سہیل بن البیضاء کے جنازہ پر مسجد ہی میں نماز پڑھی تھی۔ اس واقعہ سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ مسجد کے اندر بھی نماز جنازہ بلا کراہت جائز ہے ورنہ رسول اللہ اور فقیہ امت حضرت عائشہ مسجد کے اندر کیونکر نماز جنازہ جنازہ پڑھتے ہماری دلیل حضرت ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث ہے ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من صلى على جنازه في المسجد فلا اجرله یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے مسجد کے اندر جنازہ پر نماز پڑھی اس کے لئے کوئی ثواب نہیں ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسجد ادائے فرائض کے لیے بنائی گئی ہے پس پنج وقتہ نمازوں کے علاوہ کوئی نماز مسجد میں ادانہ کی جائے تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر جنازہ مسجد میں ہو تو اس صورت میں مسجد کے آلودہ ہونے کا احتمال ہے اس لئے بلا عذر مسجد میں میت کا لانا مکرہ ہے۔ حدیث عائشہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس زمانہ میں انصار و مہاجرین موجود تھے انھوں نے حضرت عائشہ کے عمل پر عیب لگایا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے اس وقت مسجد کے اندر جنازہ کی نماز کی کراہت معروف تھی اور رہا آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا سہیل کے جنازہ پر مسجد کے اندر نماز پڑھنا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس وقت آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم مختلف تھے آپ کے لئے مسجد سے نکنا ممکن نہ تھا تو آپ نے جنازہ کو لانے کا حکم دیا پس وہ جنازہ خارج مسجد رکھ دیا گیا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مسجد میں رہتے ہوئے نماز پڑھی اور ہمارے نزدیک اگر جنازہ مسجد سے باہر ہو اور لوگ مسجد کے اندر کھڑے ہو کر اس پر نماز پڑھیں تو کراہت نہیں ہے۔ پس اول تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کو اعتکاف کا عذر تھا دوسرے یہ کہ جنازہ مسجد میں نہیں تھا بلکہ مسجد سے باہر تھا اس لئے اس حدیث کو استدلال میں پیش کرنا مناسب نہ ہوگا۔
And funeral prayer is not performed for a deceased in a mosque in congregation because of the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is no reward for him.' And because the mosque was build for performing obligatory prayers, and because it entails the possibility of soiling the mosque. And in the case where the deceased is outside the mosque, the mashayikh differed. Translation: And funeral prayer for a deceased in a mosque in congregation is not performed because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is no reward for him.' And because the mosque was build for performing obligatory prayers, and because it entails the possibility of soiling the mosque. And in the case where the deceased is outside the mosque, the mashayikh differed. Explanation: Sahib al-Inayah, in resolving this passage, said: If only the janazah is in the mosque and the imam and some people are outside the mosque while the rest are inside, then by agreement it is not makruh. And if only the janazah is outside the mosque and the imam and all the people are inside, then the mashayikh differed: some held it is makruh and some held it is not makruh. Imam al-Shafi'i said that in no case is it makruh, i.e., even if only the janazah is in the mosque, praying over it is not makruh. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that when Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas died, Siddiqah 'A'ishah ordered that his janazah be brought into the mosque so that all the pure wives prayed over it. Then 'A'ishah said to some people around her: 'Do people criticize this action of ours?' They said yes. 'A'ishah said: 'How quickly people forget that the Messenger of Allah prayed over the janazah of Suhayl ibn al-Bayda' in the mosque.' This incident indicates that funeral prayer inside the mosque is permissible without dislike; otherwise, how would the Messenger of Allah and the jurist of the Ummah, 'A'ishah, pray in the mosque? Our evidence is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is no reward for him.' Second evidence: The mosque was build for performing obligatory prayers, so no other prayer should be performed in it. Third evidence: If the janazah is in the mosque, then there is the possibility of soiling the mosque; therefore, bringing a deceased into the mosque without excuse is makruh. The response to the hadith of 'A'ishah: At that time, the Ansar and Muhajirun were present and they criticized 'A'ishah's action. This shows that at that time the dislike of funeral prayer inside the mosque was well-known. As for the Prophet's prayer over Suhayl in the mosque, the reason is that at that time the Prophet was in i'tikaf, and he could not leave the mosque, so he ordered the janazah to be brought, and then it was placed outside the mosque, and the Prophet prayed while inside the mosque. In our view, if the janazah is outside and people stand inside the mosque and pray, there is no dislike. So first, the Prophet had the excuse of i'tikaf, and second, the janazah was not in the mosque but outside. Therefore, it is not appropriate to cite this hadith as evidence (for permissibility).
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about funeral prayer in the mosque. The Hanafi position is that it is generally makruh (disliked) to pray over a janazah inside a mosque in congregation. The text provides three proofs: (1) A hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'Whoever prays over a janazah in the mosque, there is no reward for him,' (2) mosques are built for the five daily prayers, not for funeral prayers, (3) the potential impurity (taluwih) of the mosque. The commentator clarifies exceptions: if the janazah is inside but the imam and some are outside, it is not makruh by agreement. If the janazah is outside while everyone is inside, there is ikhtilaf among scholars. Imam al-Shafi'i allows funeral prayer in the mosque absolutely, using the precedent of 'A'ishah and the Prophet's prayer over Suhayl. The Hanafi response distinguishes: 'A'ishah's action was criticized by the Companions, showing the known dislike. The Prophet's action was due to his i'tikaf, and the janazah was actually outside the mosque. Thus, the Shafi'i evidence does not negate the karahah. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is makruh tahrimi to bring the janazah into the mosque for prayer, but if the janazah is outside and the congregation is inside, it is permissible without dislike.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Dislike; the Hanafi school distinguishes between makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked, close to haram) and makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). Here it refers to the former.
جنازة (janazah): The deceased person on the bier; also refers to the funeral prayer.
اعتكاف (i'tikaf): Spiritual retreat in the mosque; a supererogatory act that requires staying in the mosque. The Prophet could not leave during i'tikaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence from 'A'ishah's action regarding Sa'd's janazah in the mosque?
A) The action is authentic and abrogates the hadith of Abu Hurayrah.
B) The Companions criticized her action, showing the known dislike.
C) The janazah was placed in the mosque because of a necessity.
D) 'A'ishah was not aware of the hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds funeral prayer in the mosque with the janazah inside as makruh tahrimi, based on the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, the purpose of mosques, and impurity concerns; the Shafi'i evidence is rebutted by contextual analysis.

Ruling on Newborn Who Cries: Naming, Washing, and Funeral Prayer
States ruling that an infant who cries after birth receives full funeral rites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an infant who shows signs of life after birth, distinguish it from a stillborn, and explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab difference regarding ghusl for a stillborn.

Core Idea
A live newborn deserves full funeral rites; for a stillborn, only respectful wrapping is obligatory, though washing is preferred.

This passage addresses a common scenario: what are the funeral obligations for an infant who dies shortly after birth? The key is whether the infant showed any sign of life (istihlal) after delivery. The Hanafi ruling is based on a prophetic hadith and distinguishes between a live-born and a stillborn. Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference between the well-known transmitted view and a preferred view on washing the stillborn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key criterion for full funeral rites
The passage uses 'istihlal' (crying or any sign of life). This is the decisive factor.
Any indication of life (crying, movement, sneezing) qualifies as istihlal in the Hanafi school.
2
State the ruling for an infant who cries
He is given a name, washed (ghusl), and funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is performed.
These acts are obligations (fard kifayah) for the community.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When a newborn cries out, pray over him; if he does not cry, do not pray over him.'
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala).
4
Note the ruling for a stillborn according to zahir al-riwayah
No ghusl, no funeral prayer; only wrapped in a cloth as an honor.
This is the well-known transmitted ruling.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
A non-zahir al-riwayah view says the stillborn should be washed because he is a soul in one respect. The commentator states this is the chosen view (mukhtar).
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is to wash the stillborn, but still no funeral prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من استهل بعد الولادة سمى وغسل وصلى عليه لقوله اذا استهل المولود صلى عليه وان لم يستهل لم يصل عليه ولان الاستهلال دلالة الحيوة فتحقق فى حقه سنة الموتى ومن لم يستهل ادرج في خرقة كرامة لبنی آدم ولم يصل عليه لماروينا ويغسل فى غير الظاهر من الرواية لانه نفس من وجه وهو المختار
ترجمہ اور جس بچہ نے ولادت کے بعد رونے کی آواز نکالی اس کا نام رکھا جائے اس کو غسل دیا جائے اور اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے ۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے جب بچہ رونے کی آواز نکالے تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے اور اگر ور نے کی آواز نکالی تواس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے اور اس لئے کہ رونا زندہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے لہذا اس کے حق میں مردوں کا طریقہ تحقیق ہوگا۔ اور جو بچہ نہیں رویا اس کو ایک کپڑے میں داخل کیا جائے اولاد آدم کی تکریم کے پیش نظر ۔ اور اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور غیر ظاہر الروایت کے مطابق اس کو نسل بھی دیا جائے۔ کیونکہ وہ من وجہ نفس ہے اور یہی حکم مختار ہے۔
تشریح استبلال صبی۔ ولادت کے وقت بچہ کا آواز بلند کرنا لیکن یہاں مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز پائی جو بچہ کی حیات پر دلالت کرے مثلا
And whoever cries out after birth, he is given a name, washed, and prayed over, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'When a newborn cries out, pray over him; and if he does not cry out, do not pray over him.' And because crying is an indication of life, so the way of the dead is established for him. And whoever does not cry out, he is wrapped in a cloth as an honor for the children of Adam, and prayer is not performed over him, because of what we narrated. And according to non-zahir al-riwayah, he is washed because he is a soul (nafs) in one respect, and this is the chosen view. Translation: And whichever child cries out after birth, his name is fixed, he is given a bath, and funeral prayer is performed over him. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When a child cries out, pray over him; and if he does not cry out, do not pray over him.' And because crying is evidence of life, so for him the way of the dead is established. And a child who did not cry is placed in a cloth for the honor of the children of Adam, and prayer is not performed over him due to the hadith we narrated. And according to non-zahir al-riwayah, he is also given a bath because he is a soul in one respect, and this is the chosen view. Explanation: Istihlal of an infant is raising the voice at birth, but here it means anything that indicates life, for example...
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding an infant who shows signs of life after birth. The key criterion is 'istihlal' — crying or any indication of life. If the infant cries (or makes any sound or movement indicating life), then he is considered a full human being: he is named, given ghusl, and funeral prayer is performed. The proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'When a child cries out, pray over him; if not, do not pray.' If the infant is stillborn (no signs of life), he is wrapped in a cloth respectfully (without ghusl or funeral prayer) according to the zahir al-riwayah. However, according to a non-zahir al-riwayah transmission, even stillborn should be washed (ghusl) because he is considered a soul in some respect. The commentator notes that this latter view is the preferred one (mukhtar). The lesson emphasizes that the decisive factor is the presence of life at birth, and the ruling varies accordingly.

Key Terms
استهلال (istihlal): Crying or any sound/vocalization by the newborn that indicates life; the original meaning is raising the voice.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six core books; the standard position.
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred ruling, often adopted by muftis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mukhtar) mentioned in the text, what should be done for a stillborn infant who did not cry?
A) He is only wrapped in a cloth, no ghusl or prayer.
B) He is given ghusl but no funeral prayer.
C) He is given both ghusl and funeral prayer.
D) He is buried without any rites.

Key Takeaway
The decisive factor for full funeral rites is any sign of life (istihlal); for a stillborn, the preferred Hanafi view is to wash but not pray.

Funeral Prayer in the Mosque: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i proof for janazah in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer in the mosque, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the evidence presented.

Core Idea
Bringing the janazah inside the mosque for prayer is makruh tahrimi; the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i proof with the hadith of Abu Hurayra and contextual analysis.

When a loved one passes away, deciding where to hold the funeral prayer can raise legal questions. The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on whether praying over the deceased inside the mosque is permissible. This lesson examines the evidence each side presents and the Hanafi response that clarifies the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What exactly is being disputed? Define the act: funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) offered with the body of the deceased present inside the mosque building.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proofs
The Hanafi school holds that it is makruh tahrimi to bring the janazah inside the mosque and pray. Three proofs are given: the hadith that such a prayer has no reward, that mosques are built for obligatory prayers, and the risk of impurity.
Note the distinction: if the body is outside the mosque, praying inside is not makruh.
3
Present the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that funeral prayer inside the mosque is permissible based on two actions: Aisha ordering Sa'd's funeral into the mosque and the Prophet praying over Suhayl's funeral in the mosque.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response contextualizes the Shafi'i evidence: Aisha's action was criticized by the Companions, indicating the ruling of dislike was known. The Prophet's case was during i'tikaf, and the body was placed outside the mosque. Therefore, these are not evidence for praying with the body inside.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Shafi'is permit without dislike; Hanafis consider it makruh unless the body is outside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنائز
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
مسجد میں ہو تب بھی اس پر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب سعد بن ابی وقاص کی وفات ہوئی تو صدیقہ عائشہ نے حکم کیا کہ ان کے جنازہ کو مسجد میں داخل کیا جائے حتی کہ اس پر تمام ازواج مطہرات نے نماز پڑھی۔ پھر حضرت عائشہ نے اپنے اردگرد کے بعض لوگوں سے کہا کہ کیا لوگوں ہمارے اس فعل پر عیب لگایا ہے۔ انہوں نے کہا کہ ہاں ( لوگوں کو اس پر اعتراض ہے ) حضرت عائشہ نے کہا کہ لوگ کس قدر جلد فراموش کر گئے کہ رسول اللہ ا نے سہیل بن البیضاء کے جنازہ پر مسجد ہی میں نماز پڑھی تھی۔ اس واقعہ سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ مسجد کے اندر بھی نماز جنازہ بلا کراہت جائز ہے ورنہ رسول اللہ اور فقیہ امت حضرت عائشہ مسجد کے اندر کیونکر نماز جنازہ پڑھتے ہماری دلیل حضرت ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث ہے ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من صلى على جنازه في المسجد فلا اجرله یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے مسجد کے اندر جنازہ پر نماز پڑھی اس کے لئے کوئی ثواب نہیں ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسجد ادائے فرائض کے لیے بنائی گئی ہے پس پنج وقتہ نمازوں کے علاوہ کوئی نماز مسجد میں ادا نہ کی جائے تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر جنازہ مسجد میں ہو تو اس صورت میں مسجد کے آلودہ ہونے کا احتمال ہے اس لئے بلا عذر مسجد میں میت کا لانا مکرہ ہے۔
حدیث عائشہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس زمانہ میں انصار و مہاجرین موجود تھے انھوں نے حضرت عائشہ کے عمل پر عیب لگایا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے اس وقت مسجد کے اندر جنازہ کی نماز کی کراہت معروف تھی اور رہا آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا سہیل کے جنازہ پر مسجد کے اندر نماز پڑھنا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس وقت آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم معتکف تھے آپ کے لئے مسجد سے نکلنا ممکن نہ تھا تو آپ نے جنازہ کو لانے کا حکم دیا پس وہ جنازہ خارج مسجد رکھ دیا گیا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مسجد میں رہتے ہوئے نماز پڑھی اور ہمارے نزدیک اگر جنازہ مسجد سے باہر ہو اور لوگ مسجد کے اندر کھڑے ہو کر اس پر نماز پڑھیں تو کراہت نہیں ہے۔ پس اول تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کو اعتکاف کا عذر تھا دوسرے یہ کہ جنازہ مسجد میں نہیں تھا بلکہ مسجد سے باہر تھا اس لئے اس حدیث کو استدلال میں پیش کرنا مناسب نہ ہوگا۔
Chapter of Funerals. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 2. If it is in the mosque, then praying over it is not makruh. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that when Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas died, Siddiqah Aisha commanded that his funeral be brought into the mosque until all the pure wives prayed over it. Then Aisha said to some people around her: 'Are people criticizing this action of ours?' They said: 'Yes (people object to it).' Aisha said: 'How quickly people forgot that the Messenger of Allah prayed over the funeral of Suhayl ibn al-Bayda in the mosque itself.' This incident shows that funeral prayer in the mosque is permissible without dislike; otherwise the Messenger and the jurist of the Ummah Aisha would not have prayed in the mosque. Our proof is the hadith of Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever prays over a funeral in the mosque has no reward.' That is, the Prophet said: Whoever prays over a funeral inside the mosque has no reward. The second proof is that the mosque is built for performing obligations, so besides the five daily prayers no prayer should be performed in the mosque. The third proof is that if the funeral is in the mosque, there is the possibility of impurity, so bringing the deceased into the mosque without excuse is makruh. The response to Aisha's hadith is that at that time the Ansar and Muhajirun were present; they criticized Aisha's action, indicating the dislike of funeral prayer in the mosque was well known. As for the Prophet's praying over Suhayl's funeral in the mosque, the reason is that at that time the Prophet was in i'tikaf and could not leave the mosque, so he ordered the funeral to be brought; it was placed outside the mosque, and he prayed while inside the mosque. In our view, if the funeral is outside the mosque and people stand inside the mosque and pray over it, there is no dislike. So firstly, the Prophet had the excuse of i'tikaf, and secondly the funeral was not inside the mosque but outside, so using this hadith as evidence is not appropriate.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding funeral prayer in the mosque. Imam Shafi'i argues it is permissible based on the actions of Aisha and the Prophet. The Hanafi school presents three proofs: a hadith that such prayer has no reward, the mosque's purpose for obligatory prayers, and the risk of impurity. They also respond to the Shafi'i evidence by noting that Aisha's action was criticized by the Companions, and the Prophet's case was due to i'tikaf with the body outside. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is makruh to bring the janazah inside the mosque, but if the body is outside and the congregation is inside, it is permissible without dislike.

Key Terms
کراہت (karahah): Dislike (makruh) in this context means the act is discouraged but not sinful; more specifically makruh tahrimi (close to haram).
جنازہ (janazah): The funeral bier with the deceased body; also the funeral prayer itself.
مسجد (masjid): A mosque, a place of worship for Muslims, particularly for the five daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it not makruh to pray janazah in the mosque?
A) When the body is inside the mosque
B) When the body is outside the mosque and the congregation is inside
C) Always when there is no impurity
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that funeral prayer with the body inside the mosque is makruh tahrimi, and the Shafi'i proof is rebutted by the context of the Prophet's i'tikaf and the Companions' criticism of Aisha's action.

Ruling on a Newborn Who Shows Signs of Life
Hanafi ruling on janazah for a newborn with signs of life

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on janazah for a newborn based on signs of life, identify the supporting hadith, and explain the intra-madhhab difference regarding ghusl.

Core Idea
A newborn who cries after birth receives full funeral rites; if no sign of life, only a dignified wrapping.

When a newborn dies shortly after birth, the Islamic funeral rites depend on whether the child showed any sign of life. The Hanafi school, using a specific hadith, distinguishes between a child with istihlal (crying or other life signs) and one without. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and a key internal debate about giving ghusl to a stillborn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling conditions
The passage discusses the legal treatment of a newborn after birth. The key factor is the presence or absence of istihlal (any sign of life such as crying, movement, sneezing). Identify that istihlal triggers a specific set of rites.
Istihlal is broader than just crying; any definitive sign of life suffices.
2
State the two distinct rulings from the matn
From the text, ascertain: (1) If istihlal occurs, the child is named, given ghusl, and janazah prayer is performed (wajib). (2) If no istihlal, the child is only wrapped in cloth and buried without ghusl or prayer, as per the primary (Zahir al-Riwayah) view.
The proof for both parts is the same hadith, as explained in the next step.
3
Locate and analyse the primary proof (dalil)
The main evidence is the hadith: 'When the newborn cries, pray over him; if he does not cry, do not pray over him.' According to Hanafi usul, the imperative 'صلى عليه' indicates wujub (obligation). The conditional clause 'إذا استهل' limits this obligation to cases with istihlal.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is considered qati by the Hanafis for this ruling.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ghusl
Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference: the Zahir al-Riwayah (Imam Muhammad's compilation) holds that if no istihlal, ghusl is not given. However, a non-Zahir transmission from Abu Yusuf states that ghusl is given even without istihlal, because the stillborn is considered a soul from one perspective (min wajhin nafs).
The author of Al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) chooses Abu Yusuf's view as the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling to a practical scenario
Synthesise: Today, the preferred Hanafi fatwa is to give ghusl to a stillborn who showed no signs of life, but not to perform janazah prayer. The child is wrapped in a shroud and buried. This balances the honour of Adam's children with the lack of established legal life.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of tarjih (preferencing) based on the reasoning of a respected Imam.
