و من استهل بعد الولادة سمى وغسل وصلى عليه لقوله اذا استهل المولود صلى عليه وان لم يستهل لم يصل عليه ولان الاستهلال دلالة الحيوة فتحقق فى حقه سنة الموتى ومن لم يستهل ادرج في خرقة كرامة لبنی آدم ولم يصل عليه لماروينا ويغسل فى غير الظاهر من الرواية لانه نفس من وجه وهو المختار
ترجمہ اور جس بچہ نے ولادت کے بعد رونے کی آواز نکالی اس کا نام رکھا جائے اس کو غسل دیا جائے اور اس پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے ۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے جب بچہ رونے کی آواز نکالے تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے اور اگر [؟] نے کی آواز نکالی تواس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے اور اس لئے کہ رونا زندہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے لہذا اس کے حق میں مردوں کا طریقہ تحقیق ہوگا۔ اور جو بچہ نہیں رویا اس کو ایک کپڑے میں داخل کیا جائے اولاد آدم کی تکریم کے پیش نظر ۔ اور اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور غیر ظاہر الروایت کے مطابق اس کو غسل بھی دیا جائے۔ کیونکہ وہ من وجہ نفس ہے اور یہی حکم مختار ہے۔ تشریح استبلال صبی۔ ولادت کے وقت بچہ کا آواز بلند کرنا لیکن یہاں مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز پائی جو بچہ کی حیات پر دلالت کرے مثلا بچہ کے کسی عضو کا حرکت کرنا یا اس کا رونے کی آواز نکالنا وغیرہ۔
بہر حال بچہ اگر پیدا ہوتے ہی مرگیا یعنی ولادت کے وقت زندگی کی کوئی دلیل پائی گئی پھر مر گیا تو اس بچہ کا نام بھی رکھا جائے۔ اس کو غسل میت بھی دیا جائے۔ اور اس پر نماز جنازہ بھی پڑھی جائے۔ دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول اذا استهل المولود صلى عليه ان لم يستهل لم يصل علیہ ہے۔ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ استہلال یعنی بچہ کا آواز نکالنا زندہ ہونے کی علامت ہے۔ لہذا اس کے حق میں مردوں کا طریقہ متحقق ہو گا۔ اور جس بچہ نے ولادت کے وقت رونے کی آواز نہیں نکالی۔ اور دوسری کوئی زندگی کی علامت بھی نہیں پائی گئی تو اس کو بطور کفن ایک کپڑے میں لپیٹ کر کسی گڑھے میں دفن کر دیا جائے۔ یہ عمل بھی فقط اولاد آدم کی تکریم کے پیش نظر ہوگا ۔ اور اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔ دلیل گذشتہ روایت ہے البتہ غیر ظاہر الروایت کے مطابق اس کو غسل دیا جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ من وجہ تو بدن کا ایک جز ہے اور من وجہ نفس ہے۔ پس دونوں کا اعتبار کیا گیا اور کہا کہ چونکہ بدن کا ایک جز اور عضو ہے۔ اس لئے اسپر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے اور چونکہ من وجہ نفس ہے اس لئے اس کو غسل دیا جائے ۔ یہی ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے اور یہی مختار قول ہے۔
A child in whom there are signs of life after birth will be named, given ghusl, and funeral prayer will be prayed over him. And whoever cries (istahalla) after birth is named, given ghusl, and prayed over, because the Prophet said: 'When a newborn cries, prayer is prayed over him; if he does not cry, no prayer is prayed over him.' And because crying is an indication of life, so the way of the dead is realized for him. And whoever does not cry is wrapped in a cloth as honor for the children of Adam, and no prayer is prayed over him according to the hadith we narrated. And according to non-Zahir al-Riwayah, he is given ghusl because he is a soul from one perspective, and that is the chosen ruling. Explanation of istihlal of a child: raising voice at birth, but here it means any sign of life such as movement of a limb or crying. So if a child dies right after birth, having shown a sign of life, he is named, given ghusl, and funeral prayer is prayed over him. The proof is the Prophet's statement: 'When the newborn cries, pray over him; if he does not cry, do not pray over him.' And rational proof: crying is a sign of life. So the way of the dead applies to him. If a child did not cry and no other sign of life is found, he is wrapped in a cloth like a shroud and buried in a pit, this is solely out of honor for Adam's children, and no prayer is prayed over him. The proof is the previous narration. However, according to non-Zahir al-Riwayah, ghusl is given. The reason: from one perspective he is a part of the body, and from another perspective he is a soul. Both are considered: because he is a part of the body, no funeral prayer; because he is a soul from another perspective, ghusl is given. That is narrated from Abu Yusuf and that is the chosen ruling.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the treatment of a newborn who shows signs of life after birth, known as istihlal (crying or any sign of life). The matn states that if the child cries (or shows life), he is named, given ghusl, and offered janazah prayer. The primary proof is the hadith: 'When the newborn cries, pray over him; if not, do not.' The rational proof is that crying indicates life, so the rulings of the dead apply. If no sign of life, the child is simply wrapped in cloth and buried out of respect, with no janazah. A secondary transmission (ghayr zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Yusuf states that ghusl is given even if no sign of life, because the child is considered a soul from one perspective, though still no prayer. This is the preferred (mukhtar) ruling in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
استهلال (istihlal): Literally raising the voice (crying). In this context, any sign of life after birth, such as crying, movement, etc.
غیر ظاہر الروایہ (ghayr zahir al-riwayah): A transmission from the Hanafi imams that is not among the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah). Often carries less weight but may be adopted as mukhtar.
من وجہ نفس (min wajhin nafs): Literally 'in one respect a soul'. Describes a stillborn or non-living child as having the essence of a soul from a certain perspective, thus deserving ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on a newborn who shows no signs of life after birth?
A) Funeral prayer is offered and ghusl is given
B) Only wrapped in cloth and buried, no prayer or ghusl
C) Ghusl is given, wrapped in cloth, and buried; no funeral prayer
D) No rites at all because he was never alive

Key Takeaway
A newborn with istihlal receives full funeral rites; one without receives ghusl (mufta bihi) and burial but not janazah prayer.

Ruling on Funeral Prayer for a Captive Child
Hanafi ruling on janazah for captive child based on parents' religion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer for a captive child in three scenarios and identify the dalil and legal maxim that determine the child's religious status.

Core Idea
A captive child's funeral prayer hinges on religious status determined by parentage or abode, not innocence.

This ruling from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical question for Muslims involved in warfare or care of captives: when is it obligatory to offer funeral prayer over a child taken captive? The answer is not based on the child's age or innocence but on his legal religious status, which is determined by his parents or, in their absence, by the land in which he is found. We will explore the three scenarios and the proof from the Prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases explicitly mentioned: (1) captive with one or both non-Muslim parents, (2) captive with parents but child professes Islam or a parent converts, (3) captive alone without parents.
Each scenario leads to a different ruling on janazah prayer.
2
Understand the principle of taba'iyyah
The child's religion follows that of his parents (taba'iyyah). The hadith 'al-walad yattabi' khayr al-abawayn dina' establishes this. 'Khayr' means the better religion, i.e., Islam over kufr.
If both parents are non-Muslim, the child is non-Muslim.
3
Apply the hadith and its exceptions
Normally no janazah for the child if with non-Muslim parents. However, two exceptions: the child himself, if sane, professes Islam (by istihsan), or one parent embraces Islam. In either case, the child becomes Muslim and janazah is prayed.
Istihsan overrides the general rule based on evidence.
4
Analyze the case of the captive alone
If the child is captured without any parent, he is presumed Muslim because the abode (Dar al-Islam) dominates. This is analogous to a foundling (laqit).
The principle is taba'iyyah al-dar (following the abode).
5
Synthesize the complete ruling
Memorize the three scenarios and the two principles: taba'iyyah al-abawayn and taba'iyyah al-dar. The hadith is the primary evidence, and istihsan allows the child's own Islam.
The practical consequence is whether the community must perform the funeral prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کوئی بچہ اپنے والدین کے ساتھ قید ہو گیا، پھر مر گیا تو نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی
واذا سبى صبى مع احد ابويه ومعالم يصل عليه لانه تبع لهما الا ان يقربا لاسلا وهو يعقل لانه صح اسلامه استحسانا اويسلم احد ابويه لانه يتبع خير الابوين دينا وان لم يسب معه احد ابويه صلى عليه لانه ظهرت تبعية الدار فحكم بالاسلام كما في اللقيط
ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی بچہ اپنے والدین میں سے کسی کے ساتھ قید ہوا اور مر گیا تو اس پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے والدین کے تابع ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ اسلام کا اقرار کرے درانحالیکہ وہ سمجھدار ہے کیونکہ استحسانا اس کا اسلام صحیح ہو گیا ہے یا اس کے والدین میں سے کوئی ایک اسلام قبول کر لے۔ کیونکہ وہ دین کے اعتبار سے خیر الا بوین کے تابع ہے۔ اور اگر اس بچہ کے ساتھ اس کے والدین میں سے کوئی قید نہیں ہوا تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے۔ کیونکہ دار السلام کے تابع ہونا اس کے حق میں ظاہر ہوا تو اس کے اسلام کا حکم دیا جائے گا جیسے لقیط میں ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی بچہ والدین میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ قید ہوا اور مر گیا تو اس پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔۔ کیونکہ بچہ والدین کے تابع ہو کر کافر ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الولد يتبع خير الابوين دينا ۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچہ دین میں اپنے والدین کے تابع ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ یہاں والدین کافر ہیں لہذا بچہ بھی کافر ہوگا اور کافر پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی نہیں جاتی اس لئے اس بچہ پر نماز جنازہ نہ پڑھی جائے ۔ ہاں اگر وہ بچہ سمجھدار ہو اور اسلام کا اقرار کر لے یا اس کے والدین میں سے کوئی ایک مسلمان ہو گیا تو اس بچہ کی نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی۔ اسلام کا اقرار کرنے کی صورت میں تو اس لئے کہ استحسانا اس کا مسلمان ہونا صحیح ہے۔ اور احد الا بوین کے تابع ہوتا ہے اور دین کے اعتبار سے خیر الا بوین وہ ہے جو مسلمان ہو گیا لہذا بچہ بھی اس کے تابع ہو کر مسلمان ہو گا۔ اور مسلمان کے جنازہ پر چونکہ نماز پڑھی جاتی ہے اس لئے اس بچہ کے جنازہ پر بھی نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔ اور اگر بچہ قید ہوا مگر اس کے ساتھ اس کے ابوین میں سے کوئی قید نہیں ہوا اور وہ بچہ مر گیا تو اس پر جنازہ کی نماز پڑھی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ
A child who is taken captive with one of his parents, then dies, funeral prayer will not be prayed over him. And if a child is taken captive with one of his parents and [dies], prayer is not prayed over him because he is dependent on them, unless he professes Islam while being sane, for his Islam becomes valid by istihsan, or one of his parents accepts Islam, because he follows the better of the two parents in religion. And if none of his parents is taken captive with him, prayer is prayed over him because the dependence on the abode (Dar al-Islam) becomes manifest, so he is judged as Muslim, like a foundling (laqit). Translation: And if a child is taken captive with one of his parents and dies, then funeral prayer will not be prayed over him because he is dependent on his parents. However, if he professes Islam while being sane, his Islam becomes valid by istihsan, or if one of his parents accepts Islam, because he follows the better of the two parents in religion. And if the child is taken captive but none of his parents is with him, then prayer is prayed over him because the dependence on the abode is manifest, so he is judged to be Muslim, as in the case of a foundling. Explanation: The scenario is that if a child is taken captive with one of his parents and dies, funeral prayer is not prayed over him because the child follows his parents and is thus a disbeliever. The Prophet said: 'The child follows the better of the two parents in religion.' This hadith shows that the child follows his parents in religion, and since the parents here are disbelievers, the child is also a disbeliever, and no funeral prayer is offered for a disbeliever. Yes, if the child is sane and professes Islam, or one of his parents becomes Muslim, then the child's funeral prayer will be offered. In the case of professing Islam, it is because his becoming Muslim is valid by istihsan. And he follows one of the parents, and the better of the two parents in religion is the one who became Muslim, so the child becomes Muslim by following him. Since funeral prayer is offered for a Muslim, his prayer will be offered. And if the child is captured but none of his parents is captured with him, and he dies, then funeral prayer will be offered over him because...
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This ruling addresses the janazah prayer for a child taken captive in war. The key principle is that a child follows his parents in religion ('the child follows the better of the two parents in religion'). If captured with one or both parents who are disbelievers, the child is considered a disbeliever and no janazah prayer is offered, unless the child himself professes Islam (if sane) or one parent embraces Islam. If the child is captured alone, without any parent, he is presumed to be Muslim because the land (Dar al-Islam) is his abode, similar to a foundling (laqit). The text provides both the Arabic ruling (matn) and Urdu commentary, emphasizing the hadith and the principle of istihsan for the child's own declaration of Islam.

Key Terms
سبی (sabi): A child taken captive in war. The ruling concerns his religious status for funeral rites.
تبعیت (taba'iyyah): Dependence or following. The child's religious status depends on his parents or the abode.
لقیط (laqit): A foundling, a child abandoned and found. Presumed to be Muslim if found in Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is funeral prayer offered for a captive child who dies?
A) Always, because children are not accountable.
B) Never, because captivity renders the child non-Muslim.
C) Only if captured without parents or if a parent converts or the child professes Islam.
D) Only if the child is over the age of puberty.

Key Takeaway
A captive child's janazah prayer depends on whether he is considered Muslim, determined by parentage, personal profession, or abode.

Funeral Rites for Newborns: The Role of Life Signs (Istihlal)
States rulings for a child born with signs of life and for one without signs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios for a newborn who dies and apply the Hanafi ruling on ghusl and janaza prayer based on the presence or absence of istihlal.

Core Idea
A newborn's first cry (istihlal) is the legal threshold for full funeral rites—without it, only respectful burial is given.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a sensitive yet clear fiqh issue: how to treat a child who dies shortly after birth. The key distinction is whether the child showed any sign of life, specifically crying (istihlal). The Prophet's hadith provides the primary proof, and the Hanafi school applies it with precision. Interestingly, a minority view within the school (Abu Yusuf) extends the obligation of ghusl even to stillborns, a ruling that many later muftis adopt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two mutually exclusive cases: (1) the child shows a sign of life (crying, limb movement, etc.), (2) the child shows no sign of life. Your first task is to recognize which scenario is being discussed and what the ruling is for each.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites a hadith: 'When a newborn cries out, pray over him; if he does not cry out, do not pray over him.' Identify this as the core textual evidence. Also note the rational proof: istihlal is a sign of life.
This is a sunnah ahad, zanni both in transmission and meaning.
3
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For a child with signs of life: name, ghusl, prayer. For a stillborn: no name, no prayer; wrapped and buried only. But note the exception: ghusl may be given per Abu Yusuf.
The default in Zahir al-Riwayah is no ghusl for stillborn.
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disagrees with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. He argues that a stillborn is both a part of the mother's body (no prayer) and a human self (deserving ghusl). This is the 'min wajh' reasoning.
The author states that Abu Yusuf's view is the chosen (mukhtar) opinion.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although the Zahir al-Riwayah position is that stillborn gets no ghusl, the commentary declares Abu Yusuf's view as mukhtar. Thus, for fatwa, the relied-upon position is that a stillborn should be given ghusl.
This is an example of Nawadir (non-Zahir al-Riwayah) becoming the operative opinion due to later tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بچہ کے کسی عضو کا حرکت کرنا یا اس کا رونے کی آواز نکالنا وغیرہ۔ ۳۶۱ باب الجنائز بہر حال بچہ اگر پیدا ہوتے ہی مرگیا یعنی ولادت کے وقت زندگی کی کوئی دلیل پائی گئی پھر مر گیا تو اس بچہ کا نام بھی رکھا جائے۔ اس کو غسل میت بھی دیا جائے۔ اور اس پر نماز جنازہ بھی پڑھی جائے۔ دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول اذا استهل المولود صلى ليرو ان لم يستهل لم يصل علیہ ہے۔ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ استبلال یعنی بچہ کا آواز نکالنا زندہ ہونے کی علامت ہے۔ لہذا اس کے حق میں مردوں کا طریقہ متفق ہو گا۔ اور جس بچہ نے ولادت کے وقت رونے کی آواز نہیں نکالی۔ اور دوسری کوئی زندگی کی علامت بھی نہیں پائی گئی تو اس کو بطور کفن ایک کپڑے میں لپیٹ کر کسی گڑھے میں داب دیا جائے۔ یہ عمل بھی فقط اولاد آدم کی تکریم کے پیش نظر ہوگا ۔ اور اس پر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے۔ دلیل گذشتہ روایت ہے البتہ غیر ظاہر الروایت کے مطابق اس کو غسل دیا جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ من وجہ تو بدن کا ایک جز ہے اور من وجہ نفس ہے۔ پس دونوں کا اعتبار کیا گیا اور کہا کہ چونکہ بدن کا ایک جز اور عضو ہے۔ اس لئے اسپر نماز نہ پڑھی جائے اور چونکہ من وجد نفس ہے اس لئے اس کو غسل دیا جائے ۔ یہی ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے اور یہی مختار قول ہے۔
A child moving any limb or making a crying sound, etc. (361) Chapter of Funerals. In any case, if a child dies as soon as it is born, i.e., at birth some sign of life was found, then it died, then this child is to be named. It is to be given a funeral bath (ghusl mayyit). And the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is to be performed over it. The proof is the saying of the Prophet (ﷺ): 'When a newborn cries out (istahal), pray over him; if he does not cry out, do not pray over him.' And the rational proof is that istihlal (the child's making a sound) is a sign of life. Therefore, for him the way of the dead will be established (i.e., funeral rites). And the child that did not make a crying sound at the time of birth, and no other sign of life was found, then he is to be wrapped in one cloth as a shroud (kafan) and placed in a pit (buried). This act is only out of respect for human offspring. And no funeral prayer is performed over him. The proof is the previous narration. However, according to non-Zahir al-Riwayah, he is to be given a bath (ghusl). The proof is that he is, from one perspective (min wajh), a part of the body (juz'), and from another perspective (min wajh), a self (nafs). So both aspects are considered. It is said: since he is a part and limb of the body, therefore no prayer is performed over him; and since he is a self (nafs) from one perspective, therefore he is given a bath. This is narrated from Abu Yusuf, and this is the chosen (mukhtar) opinion.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage addresses the funerary rulings for a newborn who dies shortly after birth. The author distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the child shows any sign of life (such as crying, moving a limb, etc.) at birth, even if it dies thereafter, it is treated as a full human being. It must be given a name, given a ritual bath (ghusl), enshrouded, and the funeral prayer (janaza) is performed over it. The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) linking istihlal (crying) to the performance of prayer. A rational proof is also provided: istihlal is a sign of life, thus all funeral rites apply. (2) If the child shows no sign of life (no cry, no movement), it is considered stillborn. It is not given a bath or prayer, but is wrapped respectfully in one cloth and buried. This is based on the same hadith. However, the author notes an exception from non-Zahir al-Riwayah (weaker transmissions): according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the stillborn should be given a bath. The reasoning is that the stillborn is both a part of the mother's body (so no prayer) and a human self (so bath required). The author states that Abu Yusuf's view is the chosen (mukhtar) opinion in this commentary. Note that the general practice in the Hanafi school is that a stillborn is not given ghusl per Zahir al-Riwayah, but many later fatwas follow Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms
استهل (istahalla): To cry out at birth; the technical term for a newborn's first cry or sound indicating life.
غير ظاهر الرواية (ghayr al-zahir al-riwayah): Transmissions that are not from the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; considered weaker.
من وجہ (min wajh): From one perspective or aspect; used to indicate that something can be considered under two different categories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for a child born with a cry but then dies?
A) No bath, no prayer
B) Bath, naming, prayer
C) Only bath, no prayer
D) Only prayer, no bath

Key Takeaway
The presence of istihlal (crying) or any sign of life triggers full funeral rites; its absence limits rites to respectful burial, though ghusl may still be given per the chosen view of Abu Yusuf.

Janaza Prayer for a Captured Child with Non-Muslim Parents
Ruling on janaza prayer for a captured child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on janaza prayer for a captured child and apply the exceptions based on the child's declaration of Islam or parental conversion.

Core Idea
A captured child's religious status follows his parents, but exceptions apply if he converts or a parent does.

In the context of jihad, a child captured alongside non-Muslim parents poses a question about his religious status. The Hanafi school rules that he follows his parents, so no janaza prayer is offered unless he or a parent becomes Muslim. This lesson unpacks the proof from hadith and the role of istihsan in validating the child's own conversion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The passage addresses the janaza prayer (funeral prayer) for a captured child. The default ruling is that if captured with at least one parent, the child is considered non-Muslim and prayer is not performed.
This is based on the principle of tab'iyyah (following).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The proof is a hadith: 'The child follows the better of the two parents in religion' (الولد يتبع خیر الابوین دینا). This indicates that the child's religion is determined by the parent who is 'better' in religion.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
If both parents are non-Muslim, the child is non-Muslim. If one becomes Muslim, the child follows that parent and becomes Muslim. The hadith is applied directly to determine the child's status.
4
Note exceptions via istihsan and conversion
Exception 1: If the child is rational and declares Islam, his Islam is valid by istihsan, so prayer is performed. Exception 2: If one parent converts, the child becomes Muslim by following the better parent. Also, if captured alone, the child is ruled Muslim due to dar al-Islam dominance (like a foundling).
Istihsan allows deviation from qiyas to avoid hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا سبى صبى مع احد ابويه ومعالم يصل عليه لانه تبع لهما الا ان يقربا لاسلا وهو يعقل لانه صح اسلامه استحسانا اويسلم احد ابويه لانه يتبع خير الابوين دينا وان لم يسب معه احد ابويه صلى عليه لانه ظهرت تبعية الدار فحكم بالاسلام كما في اللقيط ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی بچہ اپنے والدین میں سے کسی کے ساتھ قید ہوا اور مر گیا تو اس پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے والدین کے تابع ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ اسلام کا اقرار کرے درانحالیکہ وہ سمجھدار ہے کیونکہ استحسانا اس کا اسلام صحیح ہو گیا ہے یا اس کے والدین میں سے کوئی ایک اسلام قبول کر لے۔ کیونکہ وہ دین کے اعتبار سے خیر الا بوین کے تابع ہے۔ اور اگر اس بچہ کے ساتھ اس کے والدین میں سے کوئی قید نہیں ہوا تو اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے۔ کیونکہ دار السلام کے تابع ہونا اس کے حق میں ظاہر ہوا تو اس کے اسلام کا حکم دیا جائے گا جیسے لقیط میں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی بچہ والدین میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ قید ہوا اور مر گیا تو اس پر نماز جنازہ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔۔ کیونکہ بچہ والدین کے تابع ہو کر کافر ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الولد يتبع خیر الابوین دینا ۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچہ دین میں اپنے والدین کے تابع ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ یہاں والدین کا فر ہیں لہذا بچہ بھی کافر ہوگا اور کافر پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی نہیں جاتی اس لئے اس بچہ پر نماز جنازہ نہ پڑھی جائے ۔ ہاں اگر وہ بچہ سمجھدار ہو اور اسلام کا اقرار کر لے یا اس کے والدین میں سے کوئی ایک مسلمان ہو گیا تو اس بچہ کی نماز جنازہ پڑھی جائے گی۔ اسلام کا اقرار کرنے کی صورت میں تو اس لئے کہ استحسانا اس کا مسلمان ہونا صحیح ہے۔ اور احد الا بوین کے تابع ہوتا ہے اور دین کے اعتبار سے خیر الا بوین وہ ہے جو مسلمان ہو گیا لہذا بچہ بھی اس کے تابع ہو کر مسلمان ہو گا۔ اور مسلمان کے جنازہ پر چونکہ نماز پڑھی جاتی ہے اس لئے اس بچہ کے جنازہ پر بھی نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔ اور اگر بچہ قید ہوا مگر اس کے ساتھ اس کے ابوین میں سے کوئی قید نہیں ہوا اور وہ بچہ مر گیا تو اس پر جنازہ کی نماز پڑھی جائے گی
And if a child is captured with one of his parents, and with a sign of pain? it is not prayed over because he is a follower of them, unless he approaches Islam and he is rational, because his Islam becomes valid by istihsan, or one of his parents becomes Muslim, because he follows the better of the two parents in religion. And if he is not captured with one of his parents, prayer is performed over him, because the dominance of the land (dar al-Islam) becomes apparent, so he is ruled as Muslim, like the foundling (laqit). Translation: And if a child is captured with one of his parents and dies, then the funeral prayer is not performed over him, because he is a follower of his parents. Unless he declares Islam while he is rational, because by istihsan his Islam is valid, or one of his parents accepts Islam, because in religion he follows the better of the two parents. And if this child was not captured with one of his parents, then prayer is performed over him, because being subject to the land of peace (dar al-Islam) becomes apparent for him, so he is ruled to be Muslim, like the foundling. Explanation: The scenario is that if a child is captured with one of his parents and dies, then the funeral prayer is not performed over him, because the child is a disbeliever following his parents. The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'The child follows the better of the two parents in religion.' From this hadith it is understood that the child follows his parents in religion. Since here the parents are disbelievers, the child is also a disbeliever, and no prayer is performed over a disbeliever, so no prayer over this child. Yes, if the child is rational and declares Islam, or one of his parents becomes Muslim, then the child's funeral prayer is performed. In the case of declaring Islam, because by istihsan his being Muslim is valid. And he follows one of the parents, and the better of the two parents in religion is the one who became Muslim, so the child follows him and becomes Muslim. And since prayer is performed over a Muslim, therefore the child's funeral prayer is performed. And if the child was captured but none of his parents were captured with him, and he dies, then the janaza prayer is performed over him
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage addresses the janaza prayer for a child captured in war with his parents who are non-Muslims. The ruling varies based on the presence of parents and the child's own actions. There are three main scenarios: (1) If the child is captured with at least one parent, the child is considered non-Muslim by following the parents, so no janaza prayer is performed. This is based on the hadith 'The child follows the better of the two parents in religion.' However, there are two exceptions: (a) if the child is old enough to be rational (aql) and declares Islam, then istihsan validates his Islam, and prayer is performed. (b) If one of the parents converts to Islam, the child follows the parent who is better in religion (i.e., the Muslim), so he becomes Muslim and prayer is performed. (2) If the child is captured alone (without any parent), then the child is ruled as Muslim because he is in dar al-Islam and its dominance applies to him, similar to a foundling (laqit). Therefore janaza prayer is performed. The text uses istihsan for validating the child's declaration of Islam, which is a key Hanafi principle.

Key Terms
تبع (tab'a): To follow or be subject to; here it means the child's religious status is dependent on the parents.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that allows departing from qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling.
لقيط (laqit): A foundling; an abandoned child found in a place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a captured child who dies after his non-Muslim father converted to Islam?
A) Janaza prayer is not performed because the mother is still non-Muslim
B) Janaza prayer is performed because the child follows the better parent (the Muslim father)
C) Janaza prayer is performed only if the child himself converts
D) Janaza prayer is not performed because conversion must be from both parents

Key Takeaway
A captured child's janaza prayer depends on whether he is with a parent (ruled non-Muslim) or alone (ruled Muslim), with exceptions for conversion by child or parent, justified by hadith and istihsan.

Method of Carrying the Janaza and Refuting Shafi'i's View
Describes the sunnah method of carrying the funeral bier and answers Shafi'i's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of carrying the funeral bier and explain why the Shafi'i counter-argument does not override the general sunnah.

Core Idea
Four men on four corners is the general sunnah; Sa'd's case was exceptional due to angelic crowding.

Carrying the funeral bier (janaza) is a communal act of honor. The Hanafi school emphasizes a method that multiplies participants and dignity: four men each holding a corner. However, Imam al-Shafi'i cites a specific incident to argue for two carriers. This lesson unpacks the evidence and shows why the Hanafi view remains the relied-upon practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific ruling: the sunnah is to carry the bier on its four corners by four men.
The text says: 'When they carry the deceased on his bier, they take hold of its four corners. This is how the sunnah has been transmitted.'
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the Shafi'i position: two men carry it, one at front (on neck) and one at back (on chest).
Shafi'i relies on the funeral of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
Analyze the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh: it was carried by two men in that specific manner.
The Shafi'i claim is that this incident establishes the sunnah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith is contextualized by the unusual crowding of angels, making it a special case, not a general practice.
Therefore, it does not abrogate the general sunnah transmitted through the four-corner method.
5
Determine the practical difference
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi funerals, four carriers; in Shafi'i, two carriers.
The number of carriers is not a pillar of validity but a sunnah, so either method is permissible, but the Hanafi is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في حمل الجنازة ( یہ ) فصل جنازہ اٹھانے کے بیان میں ہے جنازہ اٹھانے کا بیان جنازہ اٹھانے کا طریقہ واذا حملوا الميت على سريره اخذوا بقوائمه الاربع بذلك وردت السنة وفيه تكثير الجماعة وزيادة الاكرام والصيانة وقال الشافعى السنة ان يحملها رجلان يضعها السابق على اصل عنقه والثاني على صدره لان جنازة سعد بن معاذ هكذا حملت قلنا كان ذلك لازدحام الملائكة عليه ويمشون به مسرعین دون
Chapter on Carrying the Janaza. (This) chapter is about carrying the funeral bier. The statement on carrying the janaza, the method: When they carry the deceased on his bier, they take hold of its four corners. This is how the sunnah has been transmitted. And in this is the multitude of the congregation and increase of honor and protection. And al-Shafi'i said: The sunnah is that two men carry it; the first places it on the back of his neck and the second on his chest, because the funeral of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh was carried thus. We said: That was due to the crowding of the angels upon him. And they walk briskly with it without...
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is from the section on carrying the funeral bier (janaza). The Hanafi position is that the bier should be carried by four men, each holding one of the four corners (or legs) of the bier. They argue that this is the sunnah as transmitted, and it has the added benefits of increasing the number of participants in the funeral procession and showing greater honor and care for the deceased. They then mention that Imam al-Shafi'i holds a different view: the sunnah is for two men to carry the bier, one at the front with the bier on the back of his neck, and the other at the back with the bier on his chest. Shafi'i cites the funeral of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, which was carried in that manner. The Hanafi response is that the case of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh was exceptional because the angels were crowding around him, so the human carriers had to adjust to the space. Therefore, it does not establish a general sunnah. The text then begins to mention that the bearers should walk briskly (but the passage cuts off).

Key Terms
قوائم الاربع (qawa'im al-arba'): The four corners or legs of the funeral bier.
تكثير الجماعة (takthir al-jama'ah): Multiplying the number of people in the congregation (the funeral procession).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two men, one at the front and one at the back
B) Four men, each holding a corner
C) One man carrying it alone
D) The number does not matter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of carrying the janaza on four corners is the established sunnah; the Shafi'i proof from Sa'd ibn Mu'adh is an exception, not the rule.

The Martyr (Shahid): Definition, Rulings, and the Shafi'i Dispute
Defines the martyr, lists three categories, and discusses ghusl, kafan, and salat with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the three categories of shahid according to the Hanafi school, state the rulings on ghusl, kafan, and salat al-janazah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding the funeral prayer.

Core Idea
The martyr is not washed but is prayed upon – prayer is both supplication and honor.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi definition of the martyr (shahid), who receives special rulings distinct from ordinary deceased Muslims. Unlike other deceased, the martyr is not washed (ghusl) but is shrouded and, critically, the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is performed over him. This latter point is contested by Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that the martyr's sins are erased by the sword, making prayer unnecessary. We will examine the proofs from both sides and understand the Hanafi response based on the practice of the Prophet and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of shahid
Read the definitions: (1) killed by polytheists, (2) found dead in battle with a wound, (3) killed unjustly by Muslims without diya. Understand that all share the ruling of the martyrs of Uhud.
The third category requires the instrument to be sharp, the victim adult and pure, and no financial compensation due.
2
State the agreed rulings (ghusl and kafan)
The martyr is not washed but is shrouded. The evidence comes from the Prophet's command regarding the martyrs of Uhud: 'Wrap them with their wounds and blood, and do not wash them.' Note the consensus on these points.
If the martyr has clothes, they remain; only cap, socks, and weapons are removed.
3
Identify the disputed ruling: salat al-janazah
The Hanafi school holds that the funeral prayer is fard kifayah over the martyr. Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is not performed.
This dispute is the main focus of the passage.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the sword erases sins, so there is no need for supplication or intercession. The funeral prayer is primarily a plea for forgiveness.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the funeral prayer is not only supplication but also an act of honoring the deceased. Even the sinless Prophet and children are prayed over, proving that sinlessness does not negate the obligation. Therefore, the martyr, who is honored, is even more deserving.
This response uses qiyas on the Prophet and child.

Chapter of the Martyr. Translation: The martyr is one who is killed by polytheists, or is found in the battlefield with a wound, or is killed unjustly by Muslims and no blood-money is due. He is shrouded, prayed upon, and not washed. Because such a killed person is in the meaning of the martyrs of Uhud. The Prophet said about the martyrs of Uhud: Wrap them with their wounds and blood, and do not wash them. So whoever is killed with a sharp instrument unjustly, and he is pure and adult, and no financial compensation is due, then he is also in the meaning of the martyrs of Uhud, so he is attached to them. And the effect means wound, because the wound is evidence of killing, and similarly blood emerging from an unusual place like the eye and the like. Imam Shafi'i opposes us regarding the prayer. Imam Shafi'i says that the sword erases sins, so it makes one independent of intercession. And we say that praying over the deceased is to show honor, and the martyr is more deserving. And whoever is free from sins is not independent of prayer, like the Prophet and a child. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said that there are several forms of martyr: (1) A Muslim killed by polytheists with any instrument, even wood. (2) A Muslim found in the battlefield with a wound. (3) A Muslim killed unjustly by Muslims and no blood-money is due. In these three cases, by agreement, he is shrouded, and when he is in the meaning of the martyrs of Uhud, he is not washed by consensus, but there is a difference regarding the prayer. So according to us, the funeral prayer for martyrs is performed, but according to Imam Shafi'i, it is not. The martyr is shrouded because shrouding is sunnah for the dead. If the martyr has clothes on his body, they are not removed because the Prophet said: Wrap them with their wounds and blood. In another narration: with their clothes. If he has a cap, socks, or weapons, these are removed because they are not of the type of shroud. If the shroud is insufficient, extra cloth is added. Martyrs are not washed because they are in the ruling of the martyrs of Uhud. The Prophet said: Do not wash them. A hadith states: If one is wounded in the path of Allah, on the Day of Resurrection he will come with his blood colored like blood but smelling like musk. Sahib al-Hidayah says: The one killed unjustly with a sharp instrument, being pure and adult, and no financial compensation is due, he is in the meaning of the martyrs of Uhud. So he is attached to them. Regarding the prayer, we and Imam Shafi'i differ. According to us, the funeral prayer for a martyr is fard kifayah. Imam Shafi'i does not hold that prayer is performed for the martyr. His proof: Funeral prayer is essentially intercession and supplication for the deceased, and the sword that fell upon the martyr erases his sins, so there is no need for intercession. Our response: Funeral prayer is not only supplication; it also shows honor and respect for the deceased, and the martyr is more deserving of honor. Therefore, like other deceased, the martyr's prayer is performed. And Imam Shafi'i's statement that one free from sins is independent of supplication is incorrect because who is purer than the Prophet, and an immature child is also free from sins, yet prayer is performed over both. So if prayer over the Prophet and a child is obligatory, then over the martyr it is also obligatory.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the martyr (shahid) from al-Hidayah. The author first defines the shahid in three categories based on the manner of death. The core ruling is that the shahid is not washed (ghusl) but is shrouded (kafan) and prayed upon (salat al-janazah), based on the practice of the Prophet regarding the martyrs of Uhud. The text then elaborates on the conditions: the instrument must be sharp (for the third category), the person must be pure (tahir) and adult (baligh), and no financial compensation (diya) is due. The commentary explains that the key is that the killing is unjust and for the sake of Allah. The passage then presents the prominent inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the funeral prayer. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the martyr's sins are erased by the sword, so prayer (which is intercession) is unnecessary. The Hanafi response, based on the text, is dual: (1) prayer is not merely supplication but also an act of honoring the deceased, and the martyr is most deserving of honor; (2) even the Prophet and sinless children receive funeral prayer, proving that sinlessness does not negate the obligation of prayer. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view, which holds that funeral prayer for the martyr is fard kifayah. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the ruling comes from the matn of al-Hidayah which is based on the core works of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
شهيد (shahid): A Muslim killed unjustly while fighting in Allah's cause, or killed by Muslims unjustly without diya, or found dead in battle with a wound, in the meaning of the martyrs of Uhud.
شهداء احد (shuhada' Uhud): The martyrs of the Battle of Uhud, whom the Prophet commanded to be buried without washing, wrapped in their blood and clothes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the funeral prayer over a martyr?
A) It is not performed because the sword erases sins.
B) It is performed as fard kifayah.
C) It is performed only if the martyr was killed by a sharp instrument.
D) It is performed only after washing the body.

Key Takeaway
The martyr is honored by not being washed, but the funeral prayer is still obligatory (fard kifayah) as an act of honor and supplication, following the example of the Prophet and the general rule for all deceased Muslims.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Why Hanafis Perform Funeral Prayer for Martyrs
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i exemption for martyrs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that funeral prayer for a martyr is obligatory and refute the Shafi'i objection using the concept of honor and qiyas.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is not just supplication but also honor; martyrs deserve it more.

The chapter on the martyr (shahīd) addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: should the janāzah prayer be performed for a person who died as a martyr? Imam al-Shafi'i argued that martyrs are sinless and thus need no supplication, so no prayer is required. The Hanafi response clarifies that the funeral prayer is not merely a plea for forgiveness but an act of honoring the deceased. This lesson unpacks that argument and the qiyas (analogy) used to support the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that janāzah prayer is obligatory (farḍ kifāyah) for a martyr, just like any other Muslim. The martyr is not excluded from this rite.
This is the default ruling; the burden of proof is on those who seek to exempt the martyr.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) argued that since the martyr is purified from sins by martyrdom, he does not need supplication for forgiveness; therefore janāzah prayer, which includes such supplication, is unnecessary.
The Shafi'i position is based on the purpose of prayer as du'ā for the deceased.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal is twofold: first, janāzah prayer is not only du'ā but also an act of ta'ẓīm (honor and respect) for the deceased. Second, even sinless individuals like the Prophet (peace be upon him) and an innocent child have janāzah prayer performed, proving that sinlessness does not exempt one from this rite.
The response shifts the focus from the need for forgiveness to the inherent dignity of the deceased.
4
Examine the qiyas (analogy)
The Hanafis employ qiyas jali: if the Prophet (peace be upon him) and a child (both sinless) still receive prayer, then a martyr (whose sins are forgiven but who may have had some sins) is even more deserving of honor.
The common link (illah) is not the need for supplication but the act of honoring the deceased.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, the difference is clear: Hanafis will include the martyr in the funeral prayer; Shafi'is will not. This affects funeral arrangements in mixed-madhhab communities and how scholars advise on the matter.
The ruling has implications for communal practice and the integration of different schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهيد
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
نہیں رہی۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ شہید پر نماز جنازہ نہ پڑھی جائے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ میت پر نماز جنازہ فقط دعا کے طور پر نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ دعا کے علاوہ میت کی تکریم وتعظیم کا ظاہر کرنا بھی ہوتا ہے اور شہید تکریم کا زیادہ مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے دیگر موتی کی طرح شہید کی بھی نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ جوشخص گناہوں سے پاک ہو وہ دعاسے مستغنی ہوتا ہے غلط ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے زیادہ پاک کون ہوگا اور نابالغ بچہ بھی گناہوں سے پاک ہوتا ہے۔ اس کے باوجود دونوں پر نماز پڑھنا فرض ہے۔ پس جب نبی اور صبی پر نماز پڑھنا فرض ہے تو شہید پر بھی نماز پڑھنا فرض ہوگا۔
Chapter of the martyr. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary volume 2. It is not [remaining?]. For this reason it was said that funeral prayer should not be performed for the martyr. Our response is that the funeral prayer for the deceased is not only as a supplication; rather, besides supplication, it also manifests honor and respect for the deceased, and the martyr is more deserving of honor. Therefore, like other deceased, the martyr's funeral prayer should be performed. Imam al-Shafi'i's saying that one who is pure from sins is independent of supplication is incorrect, because who is more pure than the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and a minor child is also pure from sins. Despite that, performing prayer over both is obligatory. So when prayer over the Prophet and the child is obligatory, then prayer over the martyr is also obligatory.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imām al-Shāfiʿī regarding the ruling of performing funeral prayer (ṣalāt al-janāzah) for a martyr. The text presents the Shāfiʿī objection: martyrs are free from sins, so they do not need supplication; thus no prayer. The Hanafī response explains that janāzah prayer is not merely supplication (duʿā) but also an act of honor and respect for the deceased. A martyr is even more deserving of such honor. The argument uses qiyās: if the Prophet (peace be upon him) and an innocent child—both sinless—still have their funeral prayers performed, then a martyr (who may have sins but is purified by martyrdom) is even more eligible. The Ḥanafī position is that janāzah prayer for a martyr is farḍ (obligatory), just as it is for any other Muslim.

Key Terms
شهيد (shahīd): A Muslim who is killed in the path of Allāh defending Islam, or killed by oppressors, and is granted special status in the Hereafter.
صلاة الجنازة (ṣalāt al-janāzah): The funeral prayer performed for a deceased Muslim, consisting of four takbīrs and supplications.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, why is funeral prayer performed for a martyr even though he is pure from sins?
A) Because the martyr needs supplication more than others
B) Because funeral prayer is an act of honor and respect, not just supplication
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered it specifically for martyrs
D) Because the martyr's family demands it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates janāzah prayer for martyrs because it is an act of honor, not merely supplication, and the martyr is uniquely worthy of that honor.

The Unwashed Martyr: Ruling and Proof from Uhud
Hanafi ruling with dalil from Uhud about washing martyrs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on not washing martyrs and identify the evidence from the battle of Uhud that supports it.

Core Idea
A martyr is not washed regardless of weapon; the sunnah of Uhud is decisive.

One of the unique rulings regarding martyrs is that they are not given a ritual bath (ghusl) before burial. This lesson explores the Hanafi position, which extends this status to those killed by rebels and highway robbers, using the practice of the Prophet ﷺ at Uhud as proof. We will also examine an objection and its Qur'anic response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the hukm: a martyr killed by harbis, baghis, or qutta' al-tariq is not to be washed, regardless of the weapon used.
The ruling applies to all three categories uniformly.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the sunnah of the martyrs of Uhud, where some were killed by stones and clubs, not just swords, yet none were washed.
The text says: 'لان شهداء احد ما كان كلهم قتيل السيف والسلاح'.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The key point is that the instrument of death is irrelevant; the constant practice of not washing regardless of weapon establishes the rule.
This refutes the notion that only sword-killed are martyrs.
4
Note the Objection and Response
An objection is raised: how can a victim of rebels or robbers be like the martyrs of Uhud? The response uses Qur'anic verses that command fighting rebels (49:9) and condemn highway robbers (5:33), showing the fight is for Allah's cause.
Thus, the intention and nature of the fight determine martyrdom, not the identity of the killer.
5
Evaluate the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some Shafi'is differentiate based on the weapon; Hanafis do not, following the general practice of Uhud.
The practical consequence: Hanafis never wash such martyrs; Shafi'is may in certain cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من قتله اهل الحرب او اهل البغى او قطاع الطريق فباى شىء قتلوه لم يغسل لان شهداء احد ما كان كلهم قتيل السيف والسلاح
ترجمہ اور جس کو ربیوں نے قتل کیا ہو یا باغیوں نے یا ڈاکوؤں نے کسی بھی چیز سے قتل کیا ہو اس کونسل نہ دیا جائے کیونکہ شہداء احد سب کے سب تلوار ہتھیار ہی سے قتل نہیں کئے گئے تھے۔
تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی مسلمان کو دارالحرب کے کافروں نے قتل کر دیا یا دارالاسلام کے باغیوں نے قتل کیا یا ڈاکوؤں نے قتل کیا کسی بھی چیز سے قتل کیا ہو مقتول شہید کہلائے گا اور اس کو نسل نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہداء احد سب کے سب تلوار اور ہتھیار سے مقتول نہ تھے۔ بلکہ بعض کو ان کے سر میں پتھر مار کر ہلاک کیا گیا تھا اور بعض کو ڈنڈے سے ہلاک کیا گیا تھا۔ پس یہ معلوم ہوا کہ شہید ہونے کے لئے لوہے کے آلہ سے مقتول ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ لیکن یہ اعتراض اپنی جگہ ہے کہ اہل اسلام میں سے ڈاکو یا باغی کا مقتول شہداء احد کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ان کے ہاتھوں مقتول مسلمان کو شہید نہ کہنا چاہئے ۔ جواب ہم کو جس طرح حربیوں سے قتال کا امر کیا گیا ہے۔ اس طرح باغیوں سے بھی قتال کا حکم کیا گیا ہے، چنانچہ ارشاد باری ہے فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي حَتَّى تَفِى إِلَى أَمْرِ اللهِ یعنی جو جماعت بغاوت کرے اس سے قتال کرو یہاں تک کہ اللہ کے امر کی طرف رکوع کرے۔ پس جو شخص باغی کے ہاتھوں قتل ہوا اس نے بھی اللہ کی خوشنودی کے لئے اپنی جان دیدے، پس کفار کے ساتھ جنگ کرتے ہوئے مارا جانا اور باغیوں کے ہاتھوں مقتول ہونا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اسی طرح ڈاکوؤں کے ہاتھوں سے مقتول ہونا بھی اللہ کی خوشنودی کے لئے جان دینا ہے اس لئے کہ ڈاکوؤں کے بارے میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے إِنَّمَا جَزَاءُ الَّذِينَ يُحَارِبُونَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ڈاکوؤں کو اللہ اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ محاربہ کرنے والا فرمایا ہے۔ اب جو ڈاکوؤں کے ساتھ محاربہ کرے گا اور ان کے ہاتھوں مقتول ہوگا تو گویاس نے اللہ اور رسول کی طرف سے جنگ کی اور مارا گیا اور جو شخص اللہ اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف سے ان کو راضی کرنے کے لئے جنگ کرے گا اور قتل ہو جائے گا تو وہ بھی محاربہ کفار میں مقتول کے مانند ہے، اور جو مسلمان محاربہ کفار میں مقتول ہو گیا وہ بلاشبہ شہید ہے۔ لہذا با غیوں اور ڈاکوؤں کے ہاتھ سے مقتول بھی اسی کے مانند شہید ہوگا۔
And whoever is killed by the people of war (harbis) or the people of rebellion (baghis) or highway robbers, by whatever they kill him, he is not washed because the martyrs of Uhud were not all killed by sword and weapon. ... Explanation: If a Muslim is killed by disbelievers of dar al-harb, or by rebels of dar al-islam, or by highway robbers, with whatever they kill him, the killed person is called a martyr and he should not be washed. The proof is that the martyrs of Uhud were not all killed by sword and weapon; rather, some were killed by striking stones on their heads, and some by clubs. So it is known that being killed by an iron tool is not a condition for being a martyr. But there is an objection: a person killed by robbers or rebels among Muslims is not in the sense of the martyrs of Uhud; therefore, such a Muslim should not be called a martyr. The answer: Just as we are commanded to fight against harbis, we are also commanded to fight against rebels, as Allah says: 'Fight the one that rebels until it returns to the command of Allah.' So the one killed by rebels also gave his life for the pleasure of Allah, thus being killed while fighting disbelievers and being killed by rebels are equal. Similarly, being killed by highway robbers is giving life for the pleasure of Allah, because Allah called robbers as 'fighting Allah and His Messenger.' So one who fights against robbers and is killed by them is as if he fought on behalf of Allah and His Messenger and was killed. Therefore, such a person is like one killed in fighting disbelievers, and that person is undoubtedly a martyr. Hence, those killed by rebels and robbers are also martyrs like them.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: a Muslim killed by harbis (enemy combatants), baghis (rebels), or quttāʿ al-ṭarīq (highway robbers) is considered a martyr and is not to be washed, regardless of the weapon used. The proof is the practice of the martyrs of Uḥud, where some were killed by stones and clubs, not just swords. The text then addresses an objection: why should a victim of Muslim rebels or robbers be considered a martyr like those killed by disbelievers? The response uses Qurʾānic proofs: rebels are also to be fought (Q. 49:9), and those who fight them are defending the cause of Allah. Highway robbers are described as 'waging war against Allah and His Messenger' (Q. 5:33). Thus, fighting and being killed by them is analogous to fighting disbelievers. The Ḥanafī ruling unifies the status: all such deaths make the person a martyr, and the body is not washed before burial.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the deceased; this passage rules that it is not performed for martyrs.
شهيد (shahīd): A Muslim killed in a legitimate fight for Allah's cause, including fighting rebels and robbers according to this passage.
قطاع الطريق (quṭṭāʿ al-ṭarīq): Highway robbers who fight against authority; their victims are considered martyrs if killed while resisting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Qurʾān commands fighting rebels
B) The rebel is likened to one fighting Allah and His messenger
C) The victim intended to please Allah by fighting
D) The victim used a weapon like the martyrs of Uhud

Key Takeaway
A martyr is never washed, regardless of the weapon, because the sunnah of Uhud establishes that the status depends on the cause, not the instrument.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Washing a Junub Martyr
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on washing a martyr in janabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on washing a junub martyr, distinguish between māniʿ and rāfiʿ, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Martyrdom prevents ghusl but does not remove existing janabah—Abu Hanifa distinguishes; Sahibayn do not.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: whether a martyr in a state of janābah should be washed. The debate turns on whether martyrdom is a māniʿ (preventer) or rāfiʿ (remover) of the pre-existing obligation of ghusl. We will explore the proofs from Imām Abū Ḥanīfa and the Ṣāḥibayn, and see how later Hanafi jurists settled the issue.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify that Abū Ḥanīfa holds the junub martyr must be washed, while the Ṣāḥibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) hold he should not be washed. Note that the mufta bihi is the Ṣāḥibayn's view.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf; both views are recorded in the ẓāhir al-riwāyah.
2
Analyse the Ṣāḥibayn's proof
The Ṣāḥibayn argue: (1) the obligation of ghusl due to janābah falls with death, as the deceased is no longer a legal subject; (2) martyrdom prevents a new obligation of ghusl from arising (it is a māniʿ). Thus no washing is required.
Their dalīl includes the general hadith 'bury them with their blood' and the principle that obligations end at death.
3
Analyse Abū Ḥanīfa's proof
Abū Ḥanīfa argues that martyrdom is a māniʿ of the obligation to wash the dead, but it is not a rāfiʿ of an already existing obligation. Janābah is an obligation that arose before death, so it remains. He supports this with the incident of Ḥanẓalah (ra), who was martyred while junub and washed by angels.
The key distinction is between preventing an obligation from arising (māniʿ) and removing a prior obligation (rāfiʿ).
4
Examine extensions to other cases
The same ikhtilāf applies to a menstruating (ḥāʾiḍ) or postpartum (nufasāʾ) woman who becomes pure or before cessation, and to a minor child. The Ṣāḥibayn argue the child is more deserving of honour (so not washed); Abū Ḥanīfa responds that the sword purifies sins, and a child has no sins, so the child differs from the martyrs of Uḥud.
This shows the principle is generalised beyond janābah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf and tarjīḥ
The practical consequence: Abū Ḥanīfa's view requires washing; the Ṣāḥibayn's view prohibits it. Later Hanafi jurists (e.g., in al-Hidāyah) gave tarjīḥ to the Ṣāḥibayn, making the muftā bihī that the junub martyr is not washed.
The Shāfiʿī school aligns with the Ṣāḥibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح مسئله، جنبی مسلمان اگر شہید ہو گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو نسل دیا جائے یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے اور صاحبین کے نزد یک غسل نہ دیا جائے۔ اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو غسل جنابت کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا تھاوہ موت سے ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ موت کی وجہ سے وہ غسل جنابت کا مکلف ہونے سے نکل گیا ہے اور دوسر انسل یعنی نسل میت شہادت کی وجہ سے واجب نہیں ہوا کیونکہ شہادت وجوب غسل سے مانع ہے اس لئے کہ شہداء کے بارے میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے زمـلـوهـم بكلومهم ولا
تغلسوهم حدیث میں اس کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں کہ شہید جنبی ہو یا غیر جنبی ہو۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت غسل میت واجب ہونے سے مانع تو ہے لیکن اگر پہلے سے غسل واجب ہو تو اس کو رفع کرنے والی نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ شہید کے کپڑے پر اگر نجاست لگی ہو تو اس کو دھونا ضروری ہے۔ لیکن اس کے بدن کے خون کو دھونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ پس شہادت چونکہ رافع نہیں ہے اس لئے شہادت جنابت کو بھی دور نہ کرے گی ۔ اور جب جنابت کو دور نہیں کیا تو جنبی شہید کونسل جنابت دینا واجب ہو گا۔ اس کی تائید اس واقعہ سے بھی و ہوتی ہے کہ حضرت حنظلہ جب شہید ہو گئے تو فرشتوں نے ان کو غسل دیا تھا۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کے گھر والوں سے دریافت فرمایا کہ خظلہ کس حال میں تھے ان کی بیوی نے کہا کہ مجھ سے جماع کیا تھا جب جنگ کا اعلان سناتو بغیر نسل کئے شریک جنگ ہو کر شہید ہو گئے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ یہی سبب ہے۔ یہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ بندوں کا نسل دینا واجب ہے نہ کہ ملائکہ کا۔ پس اگر شہید جنبی کو نسل دینا واجب ہوتا تو حضور خطہ کو دوبارہ نسل دینے کا حکم فرماتے ۔ جواب واجب تو فقہ نسل دینا ہے غسل دینے والا کوئی بھی ہو چنانچہ آ ملاحظہ فرمائیںکہ جب ملائکہ نے آدم کو نسل دیا تو واجب ادا ہوگیا۔ اولاد آدم نے آدم کے غسل کا اعادہ نہیں کیا۔ اگر ملائکہ کا دیا ہوا نسل ناکافی ہوتا تو اولاد آدم، آدم کے غسل کا اعدہ کرتی اور رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم حضرت حنظلہ کے غسل کا اعادہ فرماتے۔
(Arabic) And if a junub person becomes a martyr, he is washed according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said he is not washed because what became obligatory due to janabah is dropped by death, and the second washing is not obligatory due to martyrdom. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that martyrdom is known to be a preventer (mani') not a remover (rafi'), so it does not remove janabah. And it is established that Hanzalah, when he was martyred while junub, the angels washed him. And upon this difference are the menstruating woman and the postpartum woman when they become pure, and similarly before cessation according to the sound narration. And upon this difference is the child. Their (Sahibayn's) proof is that the child is more deserving of this honor. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that the sword sufficed for washing in the case of the martyrs of Uhud with the description that it is a purification, and the child has no sin, so he is not in their meaning. (Urdu translation and commentary follows...)
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Ḥanafī dispute: Imām Abū Ḥanīfa holds that a martyr who was in a state of janābah (major ritual impurity) must be washed, while the two disciples (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) say he is not washed. The text first gives the Arabic matn with proof, then elaborates in Urdu. The Ṣāḥibayn argue: (1) the obligation of ghusl due to janābah falls with death because the deceased is no longer a legal subject (mukallaf), (2) another ghusl is not obligated due to martyrdom because martyrdom prevents the obligation. Imām Abū Ḥanīfa responds: martyrdom is a preventer (māniʿ) of the obligation of ghusl for the dead, but it is not a remover (rāfiʿ) of an already existing obligation; thus janābah remains. The proof is the incident of Ḥanẓalah (may Allah be pleased with him): he was martyred while junub, and angels washed him, indicating that washing was still required. The text also extends the dispute to a menstruating or postpartum woman who becomes pure or before cessation, and to a minor child (who is not liable for sins). The Ṣāḥibayn said a child is more deserving of honor (so not washed), but Abū Ḥanīfa said the sword (martyrdom) purifies sins, and a child has no sin, so he differs from the martyrs of Uḥud. The commentary addresses an objection: if washing a junub martyr were obligatory, the Prophet would have ordered Ḥanẓalah to be washed again after the angels. The response: the obligation is fully discharged by the angels; no repetition needed, just as Adam's washing by angels sufficed.

Key Terms
جنابت (janābah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl; the text discusses whether this obligation remains upon martyrdom.
مانع (māniʿ): A preventer; martyrdom prevents the obligation of ghusl from arising (for martyrs not in janabah) but does not remove an existing obligation.
رافع (rāfiʿ): Remover; according to Abu Hanifa, martyrdom does not remove the existing obligation of ghusl from janabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa argue that a junub martyr should still be washed, despite the general rule that martyrs are not washed?
A) Because the martyr died with a fresh wound
B) Because martyrdom is a remover (rafi') of all impurities
C) Because the angels washed Hanzalah who was junub
D) Because the family of the martyr requests it

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that a junub martyr is not washed, as martyrdom drops the obligation of ghusl; the māniʿ/rāfiʿ distinction underlies the intra-school disagreement.

Does a Will for the Hereafter Break Martyrdom?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on irtithas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding irtithas from a will for otherworldly matters and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A will for a purely otherworldly matter divides the Sahibayn—Abu Yusuf sees it as seeking benefit, Muhammad does not.

This passage from the Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on what constitutes irtithas—the loss of martyr status. The specific question is whether a dying martyr's will for an otherworldly act (e.g., charity) removes his special status. The two great students of Abu Hanifa differ, and their reasoning reveals a subtle distinction between worldly benefit and acts of the dead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling context
The act is a martyr making a will for a purely otherworldly matter (e.g., charity for reward). The context is the concept of irtithas: conditions that remove the martyr's special status (e.g., not washing, shrouding, praying over).
Recall that irtithas already occurs if a martyr remains conscious past one prayer time, receives treatment, eats, etc.
2
State Imam Abu Yusuf's position and his dalil
Abu Yusuf holds that such a will constitutes irtithas because it seeks the 'comfort of reward' (rahat al-thawab), which is a form of worldly benefit.
His reasoning focuses on the intention behind the will: seeking benefit in the Hereafter still attaches to worldly concern.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and his dalil
Muhammad holds that it does not constitute irtithas because making a will is from the 'rulings of the dead' (ahkam al-mawta), not the living.
He distinguishes between actions of the living (which break martyrdom) and those of the dying/dead (which do not).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If Abu Yusuf's view is taken, the martyr loses his status and must be washed, shrouded, and prayed over. If Muhammad's view is taken, he retains his martyr status and is treated as a shahid.
This difference directly affects funeral rites.
5
Note authority and mufta bihi
The Hidayah attributes this ruling to Abu Yusuf as a narration (riwayah). The text does not give a tarjih, and later Hanafi practice may follow Muhammad's view.
This is from the nawadir (rare transmissions), not the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدا یہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ امام ابو یوسف کی روایت ہے اور اگر مقتول فی سبیل اللہ نے امر آخرت میں سے کسی چیز کی وصیت کی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ بھی ارتثاث ہے کیونکہ یہ حصول ثواب کی راحت ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک یہ ارمثاث نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مردوں کے احکام میں سے ہے۔
The author of Hidayah says that this is the narration of Imam Abu Yusuf. And if the one killed in the path of Allah makes a will for something of the matters of the Hereafter, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf this is also irtithas because it is seeking the comfort of reward. And according to Imam Muhammad, this is not irtithas because it is from the rulings of the dead.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (Ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding what constitutes irtithas (the state that removes a martyr's special status). The passage begins by stating that the author of Hidayah attributes the earlier ruling to Imam Abu Yusuf. The ruling in question is about a martyr who remains alive past the time of one prayer with his senses intact: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, this constitutes irtithas because prayer becomes a debt owed in worldly matters. Then the text presents a further case: if the martyr makes a will for a purely otherworldly matter (such as charity for reward), then Abu Yusuf considers this irtithas because it seeks benefit (comfort of reward) in the Hereafter, which is still a form of worldly concern. Imam Muhammad disagrees: such a will is from the rulings of the dead, not the living, so it does not break the martyr's status. This shows the subtle difference in their definitions: Abu Yusuf focuses on any benefit, while Muhammad distinguishes between worldly and purely otherworldly actions.

Key Terms
ارتثاث (irtithās): The state where a martyr loses his special status due to receiving worldly benefit or care, making him subject to normal funeral rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why does making a will for an otherworldly matter NOT constitute irtithas?
A) Because the martyr is still alive and his senses are intact
B) Because it is from the rulings of the dead, not the living
C) Because the will is for the comfort of reward, which is a worldly benefit
D) Because the will is invalid according to Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two views on whether a martyr's will for purely otherworldly matters causes irtithas; the practical difference is whether the body is washed or not.
